Capital and largest city of Cyprus  
This article is about the capital city of the Republic of Cyprus. For the northern part, see [North Nicosia](/wiki/North_Nicosia "North Nicosia"). For other uses, see [Nicosia (disambiguation)](/wiki/Nicosia_(disambiguation) "Nicosia (disambiguation)").

| Coordinates: [35°10′21″N 33°21′54″E﻿ / ﻿35.17250°N 33.36500°E﻿ / 35.17250; 33.36500](https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Nicosia&params=35_10_21_N_33_21_54_E_type:city(56848)) ||

**Nicosia** ,^[\[b\]](#cite_note-9)^ also known as **Lefkosia** ^[\[c\]](#cite_note-10)^ and **Lefkoşa** ,^[\[d\]](#cite_note-11)^ is the capital and largest city of [Cyprus](/wiki/Cyprus "Cyprus"). It is the southeasternmost of all [EU member states](/wiki/EU_member_states "EU member states")' capital cities.{#cite_ref-11}

Nicosia has been continuously inhabited for over 4,500 years and has been the capital of Cyprus since the 10th century. It is the last divided capital in Europe; three years after Cyprus [gained independence from British rule](/wiki/London_and_Z%C3%BCrich_Agreements "London and Zürich Agreements") in 1960, the [Bloody Christmas](/wiki/Bloody_Christmas_(1963) "Bloody Christmas (1963)") conflict between [Greek Cypriots](/wiki/Greek_Cypriots "Greek Cypriots") and [Turkish Cypriots](/wiki/Turkish_Cypriots "Turkish Cypriots") triggered island-wide [intercommunal violence](/wiki/Cypriot_intercommunal_violence#Crisis_of_1963–1964 "Cypriot intercommunal violence"), and Nicosia's Greek Cypriot and Turkish Cypriot communities segregated into its south and [north](/wiki/North_Nicosia "North Nicosia") respectively in 1964. A decade later, [Turkey invaded Cyprus](/wiki/Turkish_invasion_of_Cyprus "Turkish invasion of Cyprus") following [Greece's successful attempt](/wiki/1974_Cypriot_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "1974 Cypriot coup d'état") to [take over the island](/wiki/Enosis "Enosis"). The leaders of the takeover would later step down, but the dividing line running through Nicosia (and the rest of the island, interrupted only briefly by [British military bases](/wiki/Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia "Akrotiri and Dhekelia")) became a [demilitarised zone](/wiki/Demilitarized_zone "Demilitarized zone") that remains under the control of Cyprus while heavily policed by the [United Nations](/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations"); it is now known as the [United Nations Buffer Zone in Cyprus](/wiki/United_Nations_Buffer_Zone_in_Cyprus "United Nations Buffer Zone in Cyprus") between the Republic of Cyprus, which is internationally [recognised](/wiki/Diplomatic_recognition "Diplomatic recognition"), and [Northern Cyprus](/wiki/Northern_Cyprus "Northern Cyprus"), which is recognised only by Turkey. The ongoing dispute between the two communities is known as the [Cyprus problem](/wiki/Cyprus_problem "Cyprus problem").

Apart from its legislative and administrative functions, Nicosia has established itself as the island's financial capital and its main international business centre.^[\[8\]](#cite_note-12)^ In 2018, Nicosia was the 32nd richest city in the world in relative purchasing power.^[\[9\]](#cite_note-13)^ In the 2022 [GaWC](/wiki/Globalization_and_World_Cities_Research_Network "Globalization and World Cities Research Network") ranking, Nicosia was classified as a "Beta **−** " city ( '[global city](/wiki/Global_city "Global city")').^[\[10\]](#cite_note-14)^{#cite_ref-14}  

Names {#Toponymy}
-----------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=1 "Edit section: Names")\]

The earliest mention of the city is on a clay prism^\[*[clarification needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify "Wikipedia:Please clarify")*\]^ of the [Assyrian](/wiki/Assyrian_Empire "Assyrian Empire") [king](/wiki/List_of_emperors_of_Assyria "List of emperors of Assyria") [Esarhaddon](/wiki/Esarhaddon "Esarhaddon") dated to 672 BC, which calls it Lidir.^\[*[clarification needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify "Wikipedia:Please clarify")*\]^ The local form of the name was later variously [hellenized](/wiki/Hellenization_of_place_names "Hellenization of place names") as **Ledra** ([Ancient Greek](/wiki/Ancient_Greek_language "Ancient Greek language"): Λήδρα, *Lḗdra* ),^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ Ledrae (Λέδραι, *Lédrai* ),^[\[11\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHill1939379-15)^ Ledroi (Λήδροι, *Lḗdroi* ),^[\[12\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMichaelides_&_al.2012-16)^ and Ledron (Λεδρῶν, *Ledrō̂n* , and Λῆδρον, *Lē̂dron* ).^[\[11\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHill1939379-15)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHill1939379_15-1}

By [late antiquity](/wiki/Late_antiquity "Late antiquity"), [early Christian sources](/wiki/Early_Christianity "Early Christianity") were recording the location as Leuteon (Λευτεῶν, *Leuteō̂n* ) and as Leucon (Λευκῶν, *Leukō̂n* ),^[\[13\]](#cite_note-sternburg-17)^ Leucotheon (Λευκοθέον, *Leukothéon* ), Leucoi Theoi (Λευκοί Θεοί, *Leukoí Theoí* ),^[\[11\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHill1939379-15)^ and Leucopolis (Λευκούπολις, *Leukoúpolis* ),^[\[14\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHill1939380-18)^ incorporating forms of the [Greek](/wiki/Ancient_Greek_language "Ancient Greek language") words for "white" ([λευκός](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CE%BB%CE%B5%CF%85%CE%BA%CF%8C%CF%82 "wikt:λευκός"), *leukós* ) or "[poplar](/wiki/Populus "Populus")" ([λεύκη](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CE%BB%CE%B5%CF%8D%CE%BA%CE%B7 "wikt:λεύκη"), *leúkē* ) and for "[God](/wiki/God_the_Father "God the Father")" ([Θεός](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CE%98%CE%B5%CF%8C%CF%82 "wikt:Θεός"), *Theós* ), "[god](/wiki/Greek_gods "Greek gods")" ([θεός](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CE%B8%CE%B5%CF%8C%CF%82 "wikt:θεός"), *theós* ), or "[goddess](/wiki/Greek_goddesses "Greek goddesses")" ([θεᾱ́](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CE%B8%CE%B5%E1%BE%B1%CC%81 "wikt:θεᾱ́"), *theá* ), with possible allusion to a supposed son of [Ptolemy I Soter](/wiki/Ptolemy_I_Soter "Ptolemy I Soter")^[\[11\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHill1939379-15)^ or to the [sea goddess](/wiki/Sea_goddess "Sea goddess") [Leucothea](/wiki/Leucothea "Leucothea"). During the [Byzantine period](/wiki/Byzantine_Empire "Byzantine Empire"), the form **Leucosia** (Λευκουσία, *Leukousía* )---usually parsed as intending "the white estate" ([ἡ](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E1%BC%A1 "wikt:ἡ") [λευκή](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CE%BB%CE%B5%CF%85%CE%BA%CE%AE "wikt:λευκή") [οὐσία](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CE%BF%E1%BD%90%CF%83%CE%AF%CE%B1 "wikt:οὐσία"), *hē leukḗ ousía* )---became common;^[\[15\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPapacostas201287–88-19)^ this developed into [modern Greek](/wiki/Modern_Greek_language "Modern Greek language") Lefkosia (Λευκωσία, *Lefkosía* , [\[lefkoˈsi.a\]](/wiki/Help:IPA/Greek "Help:IPA/Greek"))^[\[16\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHill1939380–381-20)^ and [Turkish](/wiki/Turkish_language "Turkish language") Lefkoşa ([\[lefˈkoʃa\]](/wiki/Help:IPA/Turkish "Help:IPA/Turkish")).{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHill1939380–381_20-0}

The [Latin](/wiki/Latin_language "Latin language") and [English](/wiki/English_language "English language") name Nicosia appeared under the medieval [Crusader](/wiki/Crusades "Crusades") [Lusignan dynasty](/wiki/House_of_Lusignan "House of Lusignan"),^[\[14\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHill1939380-18)^^[\[17\]](#cite_note-21)^ around the same time the Cypriot port [Limassol](/wiki/Limassol "Limassol") replaced its previous initial N with an L for similarly unknown reasons.^[\[18\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHill1939376–377-22)^ [Hill](/wiki/Sir_George_Hill "Sir George Hill") provides several other examples of interchanging /l/ and /n/ as far back as the [Phoenician Cypriots](/wiki/Phoenician_Cyprus "Phoenician Cyprus"), suggesting the exchange may have arisen from a variable native pronunciation.^[\[18\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHill1939376–377-22)^ The name is also preserved as the [Armenian](/wiki/Armenian_language "Armenian language") **Nikosia** (Նիկոսիա) and the [Cypriot Arabic](/wiki/Cypriot_Arabic "Cypriot Arabic") **Nikusiya** .^[\[19\]](#cite_note-23)^^[\[20\]](#cite_note-24)^^\[*[clarification needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify "Wikipedia:Please clarify")*\]^{#cite_ref-24}

The town also appears as Callinicesis (Καλλινικησις, *Kallinikēsis* , or Καλλινεικησις, *Kallineikēsis* ) in some of the [hagiographies](/wiki/Hagiographies "Hagiographies") concerning the saints [Tryphillius](/wiki/Saint_Tryphillius "Saint Tryphillius") and [Spyridon](/wiki/Saint_Spyridon "Saint Spyridon") ( 4th century).^[\[21\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHill1939379–380-25)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHill1939379–380_25-0}  

History {#History}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=2 "Edit section: History")\]  
For a chronological guide, see [Timeline of Nicosia](/wiki/Timeline_of_Nicosia "Timeline of Nicosia").  

### Prehistoric Nicosia {#Prehistoric_Nicosia}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=3 "Edit section: Prehistoric Nicosia")\]  
Main article: [Ledra](/wiki/Ledra "Ledra")

Nicosia has been in continuous habitation since around 2500 BC near the beginning of the [Bronze Age](/wiki/Bronze_Age "Bronze Age"), when the first inhabitants settled in the fertile plain of Mesaoria.^[\[22\]](#cite_note-26)^{#cite_ref-26}

The [city-state](/wiki/City-state "City-state") of [Ledra](/wiki/Ledra "Ledra") is similarly connected with the area of Nicosia, although the larger share of [Mycenaean-era](/wiki/Mycenaean_Greece "Mycenaean Greece") ruins in the area are at the broad hill of Ayia Paraskevi or Leondari Vounò 6 km (3.7 mi) southeast of central Nicosia.^[\[11\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHill1939379-15)^ Ledra is reported as one of the twelve kingdoms of ancient Cyprus built by [Achaeans](/wiki/Achaeans_(tribe) "Achaeans (tribe)") after the end of the [Trojan War](/wiki/Trojan_War "Trojan War").^[\[23\]](#cite_note-27)^ The kingdom was quickly destroyed. The Cypriot vassal state transcribed as "Lidir" in a 672 BC Assyrian text is generally identified with the remains which have been found nearer to the modern city.^[\[11\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHill1939379-15)^ Its ruler Onasagoras^\[*[clarification needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify "Wikipedia:Please clarify")*\]^ was recorded paying tribute to the [Assyrian](/wiki/Assyrian_Empire "Assyrian Empire") [king](/wiki/List_of_Assyrian_emperors "List of Assyrian emperors") [Esarhaddon](/wiki/Esarhaddon "Esarhaddon").{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHill1939379_15-5}  

### Ancient Nicosia {#Ancient_Nicosia}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=4 "Edit section: Ancient Nicosia")\]

By 330 BC, Ledra was recorded to be a small unimportant town.^[\[24\]](#cite_note-28)^ It is thought that the settlement was economically and politically dependent on the nearby town of [Chytri](/wiki/Chytri "Chytri").^[\[25\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMichaelides_&_al.201252-29)^ The main activity of the town inhabitants was farming. During this era, Ledra did not have the huge growth that the other Cypriot coastal towns had, which was primarily based on trade.^[\[26\]](#cite_note-30)^ Some sources record that it was restored and improved by Leucos, son of [Ptolemy I Soter](/wiki/Ptolemy_I_Soter "Ptolemy I Soter") of [Egypt](/wiki/Ptolemaid_Egypt "Ptolemaid Egypt") around 280 BC,^[\[27\]](#cite_note-31)^^[\[13\]](#cite_note-sternburg-17)^ although [Hill](/wiki/Sir_George_Hill "Sir George Hill") considered this an early modern "fancy" based solely on pseudoetymological speculations.^[\[11\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHill1939379-15)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHill1939379_15-6}

In the 4th century, the town was the seat of a bishopric under the name Ledron, Leuteon, or Leucotheon. Its bishop [St Tryphillius](/wiki/Saint_Tryphillius "Saint Tryphillius") was a student of [St Spyridon](/wiki/Saint_Spyridon "Saint Spyridon").^[\[28\]](#cite_note-32)^ Archaeological evidence indicates that the town regained much of its earlier significance in the early Christian period,^[\[29\]](#cite_note-which_is_abut_58_secs_long_demetrios4-33)^ and the presence of two or three [basilicas](/wiki/Basilica "Basilica") with *[opus sectile](/wiki/Opus_sectile "Opus sectile")* decorations, along with marbles decorated with high relief indicate the presence of a relatively prosperous and sophisticated Christian society.^[\[30\]](#cite_note-34)^{#cite_ref-34}  

### Medieval Nicosia {#Medieval_Nicosia}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=5 "Edit section: Medieval Nicosia")\]

After the destruction of Cyprus's capital [Salamis](/wiki/Salamis,_Cyprus "Salamis, Cyprus") by Arab raids in 647, along with extensive damage to other coastal settlements, the economy of the island became much more inward-looking and inland towns gained relative significance. Nicosia benefited from this and functioned as an outlet of the agricultural products from its hinterland, the [Mesaoria](/wiki/Mesaoria "Mesaoria") plain. It further was at an advantageous position due to its ample water supply. As such, the town developed enough for the [Byzantine Empire](/wiki/Byzantine_Empire "Byzantine Empire") to choose Nicosia as the capital of the island around 965, when the [Byzantine navy](/wiki/Byzantine_navy "Byzantine navy") restored full Byzantine control over the island and it was organized as a [theme of the empire](/wiki/Theme_of_Cyprus "Theme of Cyprus").^[\[31\]](#cite_note-35)^ The Byzantines moved the island's administration seat to Nicosia primarily for security reasons as coastal towns were often suffering from raids. From that point on it has remained as the capital of Cyprus and was the seat of the Byzantine governor of Cyprus. The last such governor was [Isaac Komnenos](/wiki/Isaac_Komnenos_of_Cyprus "Isaac Komnenos of Cyprus"), who declared himself emperor on the island and ruled it from 1183 to 1191.^[\[32\]](#cite_note-36)^ Testimony as late as 1211 indicates that Nicosia was not a walled city at that point and thus that the Byzantines did not build a city wall, thinking that the city's inland location would be sufficient for defense purposes. The Byzantines did, however, build a relatively weak fort within the city.^[\[33\]](#cite_note-37)^ The economy under Byzantine rule consisted mostly of the trading of agricultural goods, but the town also produced luxury items and metalware due to the presence of the imperial administration.^[\[34\]](#cite_note-38)^{#cite_ref-38}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Selimiye_Mosque_%28St._Sophie_Cathedral%29_%2836%29.JPG/220px-Selimiye_Mosque_%28St._Sophie_Cathedral%29_%2836%29.JPG)](/wiki/File:Selimiye_Mosque_(St._Sophie_Cathedral)_(36).JPG) St. Sophia Cathedral, which was built during rule by the [House of Lusignan](/wiki/House_of_Lusignan "House of Lusignan") and later converted into the [Selimiye Mosque](/wiki/Selimiye_Mosque,_Nicosia "Selimiye Mosque, Nicosia"), exemplifies the [Gothic architecture](/wiki/Gothic_architecture "Gothic architecture") in Nicosia. [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Venetian_walls_and_green_parks_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus_Kypros.jpg/220px-Venetian_walls_and_green_parks_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus_Kypros.jpg)](/wiki/File:Venetian_walls_and_green_parks_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus_Kypros.jpg) [Venetian walls of Nicosia](/wiki/Venetian_walls_of_Nicosia "Venetian walls of Nicosia")

On his way to the [Holy Land](/wiki/Holy_Land "Holy Land") during the [Third Crusade](/wiki/Third_Crusade "Third Crusade") in 1187, [Richard I of England](/wiki/Richard_I_of_England "Richard I of England")'s fleet was plagued by storms, making him to stop first at [Crete](/wiki/Crete "Crete") and then at [Rhodes](/wiki/Rhodes "Rhodes"). Three ships continued on, one of which was carrying [Joan of England, Queen of Sicily](/wiki/Joan_of_England,_Queen_of_Sicily "Joan of England, Queen of Sicily") and [Berengaria of Navarre](/wiki/Berengaria_of_Navarre "Berengaria of Navarre"), Richard's bride-to-be. Two of the ships were wrecked off Cyprus, but the ship bearing Joan and Berengaria made it safely to [Limassol](/wiki/Limassol "Limassol"). Joan refused to come ashore, fearing she would be captured and held hostage by [Isaac Komnenos of Cyprus](/wiki/Isaac_Komnenos_of_Cyprus "Isaac Komnenos of Cyprus"), who hated all Franks. Her ship sat at anchor for a full week before Richard finally arrived on 8 May. Outraged at the treatment of his sister and his future bride, Richard invaded.^[\[35\]](#cite_note-39)^^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ Richard laid siege to Nicosia, finally met and defeated Isaac Komnenos at [Tremetousia](/wiki/Tremetousia "Tremetousia") and became ruler of the island, but sold it to the [Knights Templar](/wiki/Knights_Templar "Knights Templar").{#cite_ref-39}

The Frankish rule of Cyprus started from 1192 and lasted until 1489. During this time, Nicosia was the capital of the medieval [Kingdom of Cyprus](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Cyprus "Kingdom of Cyprus"), the seat of [Lusignan](/wiki/Lusignan "Lusignan") kings, the Latin Church and the Frankish administration of the island. During the Frankish rule, the walls of the city were built along with many other palaces and buildings, including the gothic [St. Sophia Cathedral](/wiki/St._Sophia_Cathedral,_Nicosia "St. Sophia Cathedral, Nicosia"). The tombs of the [Lusignan kings](/wiki/House_of_Lusignan "House of Lusignan") can be found there.
[![Image of map of Nicosia, created in 1597](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Nicosia_by_Giacomo_Franco.jpg/220px-Nicosia_by_Giacomo_Franco.jpg)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_by_Giacomo_Franco.jpg) Map of Nicosia in Cyprus, created in 1597 [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Nicosia_01-2017_img08_Famagusta_Gate.jpg/220px-Nicosia_01-2017_img08_Famagusta_Gate.jpg)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_01-2017_img08_Famagusta_Gate.jpg) [Famagusta Gate](/wiki/Famagusta_Gate "Famagusta Gate") built in 1567

In 1373/4, Nicosia was occupied and ravaged by the [Republic of Genoa](/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa "Republic of Genoa") and in 1426 from the [Mamluk Sultanate](/wiki/Mamluk_Sultanate_(Cairo) "Mamluk Sultanate (Cairo)").^[\[36\]](#cite_note-40)^{#cite_ref-40}

In 1489, when Cyprus came under the rule of the [Republic of Venice](/wiki/Republic_of_Venice "Republic of Venice"), Nicosia became their administrative centre and the seat of the Republic. The Venetian Governors saw it as a necessity for all the cities of Cyprus to be fortified due to the Ottoman threat.^[\[37\]](#cite_note-41)^ In 1567 Venetians built the new fortifications of Nicosia, which are well-preserved still to this day, demolishing the old walls built by the [Franks](/wiki/Franks "Franks") as well as other important buildings of the Frankish era including the King's Palace, other private palaces and churches and monasteries of both Orthodox and Latin Christians.^[\[38\]](#cite_note-nicosia.org.cy-42)^ The new walls took the shape of a star with eleven bastions. The design of the bastion is more suitable for artillery and a better control for the defenders. The walls have three gates, to the North [Kyrenia Gate](/wiki/Kyrenia_Gate "Kyrenia Gate"), to the west Paphos Gate and to the east [Famagusta Gate](/wiki/Famagusta_Gate "Famagusta Gate").^[\[38\]](#cite_note-nicosia.org.cy-42)^ The river [Pedieos](/wiki/Pedieos "Pedieos") used to flow through the Venetian walled city. In 1567 it was later diverted outside onto the newly built moat for strategic reasons, due to the expected Ottoman attack.^[\[39\]](#cite_note-liminalzones.kein.org-43)^{#cite_ref-liminalzones.kein.org_43-0}  

### Ottoman rule {#Ottoman_rule}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=6 "Edit section: Ottoman rule")\]
[![Photo of old city aqueduct in Nicosia](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Nicosia_01-2017_img04_aqueduct.jpg/220px-Nicosia_01-2017_img04_aqueduct.jpg)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_01-2017_img04_aqueduct.jpg) The [Nicosia aqueduct](/wiki/Nicosia_aqueduct "Nicosia aqueduct") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Nicosia._%281878%29_-_TIMEA.jpg/220px-Nicosia._%281878%29_-_TIMEA.jpg)](/wiki/File:Nicosia._(1878)_-_TIMEA.jpg) View of Nicosia in 1878

On 1 July 1570, the city came under the rule of the [Ottomans](/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire"). On 22 July, [Piyale Pasha](/wiki/Piyale_Pasha "Piyale Pasha") having captured Paphos, [Limassol](/wiki/Limassol "Limassol") and Larnaca marched his army towards Nicosia and laid siege to the city.^[\[40\]](#cite_note-44)^ The city managed to last 40 days under siege until its fall on 9 September 1570. The story of the Cypriot martyr [Arnaude de Rocas](/wiki/Arnaude_de_Rocas "Arnaude de Rocas") dates from the fall of Nicosia. Some 20,000 residents died during the siege and every church, public building, and palace was looted.^[\[41\]](#cite_note-45)^ Nicosia had an estimated population of 21,000 before the Ottoman conquest, and based on the Ottoman census data of 1572, the population had been reduced to 1,100--1,200. The devastation of the city was so extensive that for the few years after the conquest, a number of villages in the island had a larger population than Nicosia.^[\[42\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTETheocharides_&_al.2012237-46)^^[\[43\]](#cite_note-47)^ The main Latin churches were converted into mosques, such as the conversion of the Saint Sophia Cathedral.{#cite_ref-47}

Nicosia was the seat of the [Pasha](/wiki/Pasha "Pasha"), the [Greek Archbishop](/wiki/Church_of_Cyprus "Church of Cyprus"), the [Dragoman](/wiki/Dragoman "Dragoman") and the [Qadi](/wiki/Qadi "Qadi"). The *Palazzo del Governo* of Venetian times became the seat of the Pasha, the governor of Cyprus, and the building was renamed as the Konak or Seraglio (Saray). The square outside was known as Seraglio Square or Sarayonu (literally front of the Saray), as it is known to the present day. The saray was demolished in 1904 and the present block of Government Offices built on the site.^[\[44\]](#cite_note-jeffery-48)^{#cite_ref-jeffery_48-0}

When the newly settled Turkish population arrived they generally lived in the north of the old riverbed. Greek Cypriots remained concentrated in the south, where the [Archbishopric](/wiki/Archbishopric "Archbishopric") of the Orthodox Church was built. Other ethnic minority groups such as the Armenians and Latins came to be settled near the western entry into the city at Paphos Gate.^[\[45\]](#cite_note-49)^{#cite_ref-49}

The names of the 12 quarters into which Nicosia was originally divided at the time of the Ottoman Conquest are said to be derived from the 12 generals in command of divisions of the Ottoman army at the time. Each general being posted to a quarter, that quarter (with two exceptions) was known by his name as follows:

1. General Ibrahim Pasha.
2. General Mahmoud Pasha.
3. General Ak Kavuk Pasha. (This is a nickname meaning "white cap".)
4. General Koukoud Effendi.
5. General Arab Ahmed Pasha.
6. General Abdi Pasha, known as Chavush (Sergeant) from which rank he was probably promoted.
7. General Haydar Pasha.
8. General Karamanzade (son of a Caramanian, other names not given).
9. General Yahya Pasha (now known as the Phaneromeni Quarter).
10. General Daniel Pasha (name of quarter changed subsequently to Omerie in honor of the Caliph Omar who stayed there for a night when in Cyprus).
11. Tophane (Artillery Barracks)
12. Nebetkhane, meaning police station or quarters of the patrol.^[\[44\]](#cite_note-jeffery-48)^{#cite_ref-jeffery_48-1}

The names of the generals in command of the last two-quarters have been lost:

Later the number of neighborhoods was increased to 24. Each neighborhood was organized around a mosque or a church, where mainly the respective Muslim and Christian communities lived.^[\[46\]](#cite_note-Coexistence-50)^{#cite_ref-Coexistence_50-0}  

### British rule {#British_rule}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=7 "Edit section: British rule")\]
[![Painting, hoisting the British flat in Nicosia](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Hosting_the_British_flag_at_Nicosia.jpg/170px-Hosting_the_British_flag_at_Nicosia.jpg)](/wiki/File:Hosting_the_British_flag_at_Nicosia.jpg) Hoisting the British flag in Nicosia {#cite_ref-Cyprus_51-0}

| Year |        |        |
| 1881 | 11,536 |  ---   |
| 1891 | 12,515 | +8.5%  |
| 1901 | 14,481 | +15.7% |
| 1911 | 16,052 | +10.8% |
| 1921 | 11,831 | −26.3% |
| 1931 | 23,324 | +97.1% |
| 1946 | 34,485 | +47.9% |
| 1960 | 45,629 | +32.3% |
|------|--------|--------|
| Source for 1881--1960.^[\[47\]](#cite_note-Cyprus-51)^ |||
[Historical population]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/1914_Nicosia_Cyprus.png/220px-1914_Nicosia_Cyprus.png)](/wiki/File:1914_Nicosia_Cyprus.png) View of Nicosia in 1914

Nicosia came under the rule of [the United Kingdom](/wiki/British_Empire "British Empire") on 5 July 1878 in consequence of the [Cyprus Convention](/wiki/Cyprus_Convention "Cyprus Convention"),^[\[48\]](#cite_note-52)^ in exchange for its support of the [Ottoman Empire](/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire") during the [Congress of Berlin](/wiki/Congress_of_Berlin "Congress of Berlin").{#cite_ref-52}

The old Ottoman administrative headquarters (the Saray) was replaced in 1904 by a new building containing Law Courts, the Land Registry, and the Forestry, Customs, and Nicosia Commissioner's Offices.^[\[44\]](#cite_note-jeffery-48)^ Adjacent was the Nicosia Police headquarters, while opposite were the General Post Office and the Telegraph Office.^[\[49\]](#cite_note-53)^ A Venetian Column, previously in a fenced courtyard near the Saray,^[\[50\]](#cite_note-54)^ was restored on a new site in the summer of 1915 in the middle of Saray Square. The Nicosia column was presumably erected in compliment to the reigning Doge Francesco Donati about the year 1550.^[\[44\]](#cite_note-jeffery-48)^{#cite_ref-jeffery_48-3}

Just after the British Occupation a Municipal Council was constituted in Nicosia in 1882 for the general administration of public affairs within the city and for a certain area without the walls, under the presidency of a Mayor.^[\[44\]](#cite_note-jeffery-48)^ The first municipal offices were in Municipality Square (now the central municipal market), but in 1944 the offices were transferred temporarily to the d'Avila bastion and in 1952 this was made permanent with a decision to renovate the building.^[\[51\]](#cite_note-55)^{#cite_ref-55}
[![Extensions to the Nicosia municipal area](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Nicosia_boundary_extensions.png/300px-Nicosia_boundary_extensions.png)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_boundary_extensions.png) Extensions to the Nicosia municipal area

In 1923 the municipal limits were extended further (see map) and this new area was divided among several of the existing intramural neighborhoods.^[\[52\]](#cite_note-56)^ In 1938 the boundary was extended to the present limits in the west and to the boundaries of Ayii Omoloyites, Palouriotissa, Kaimakli and Omorfita.^[\[53\]](#cite_note-nicexpand2-57)^ In 1944 the village authority of Ayii Omoloyites was absorbed, then, shortly after independence, Palouriotissa, Kaimakli and Omorfita were annexed to the city in 1968.^[\[54\]](#cite_note-58)^{#cite_ref-58}

[Nicosia International Airport](/wiki/Nicosia_International_Airport "Nicosia International Airport") was opened in 1947. It remained the location for the Air Station until its abandonment in 1974.

In 1955 an armed struggle against British rule began aiming to unite the island with Greece, [Enosis](/wiki/Enosis "Enosis"). The struggle was led by EOKA, a [Greek Cypriot](/wiki/Greek_Cypriot "Greek Cypriot") nationalist military resistance organization,^[\[55\]](#cite_note-59)^ and supported by the vast majority of Greek Cypriots. The unification with Greece failed and instead the independence of Cyprus was declared in 1960. During the period of the struggle, Nicosia was the scene of violent protests against British rule.^[\[56\]](#cite_note-60)^^[\[57\]](#cite_note-61)^{#cite_ref-61}  

### Independence and division {#Independence_and_division}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=8 "Edit section: Independence and division")\]  
See also: [Modern history of Cyprus](/wiki/Modern_history_of_Cyprus "Modern history of Cyprus")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Nicosia_Eleftheria_Ariadnis_Street_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg/220px-Nicosia_Eleftheria_Ariadnis_Street_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_Eleftheria_Ariadnis_Street_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg) Scheme for new pedestrianized streets in old Nicosia implemented after 2004 [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Nicosia%2C_Cyprus_%2837581219510%29.jpg/220px-Nicosia%2C_Cyprus_%2837581219510%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Nicosia,_Cyprus_(37581219510).jpg) Street in Nicosia close to the buffer zone

In 1960, Nicosia became the capital of the [Republic of Cyprus](/wiki/Cyprus "Cyprus"), a state established by the Greek and Turkish Cypriots. In 1963, the Greek Cypriot side proposed amendments to the constitution, which were rejected by the Turkish Cypriot community.^[\[58\]](#cite_note-62)^ During the aftermath of this crisis, on 21 December 1963, [intercommunal violence](/wiki/Cypriot_intercommunal_violence "Cypriot intercommunal violence") broke out between Greek and Turkish Cypriots. Nicosia was divided into Greek and Turkish Cypriot quarters with the [Green Line](/wiki/Green_Line_(Cyprus) "Green Line (Cyprus)"), named after the color of the pen used by the [United Nations](/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations") officer to draw the line on a map of the city.^[\[59\]](#cite_note-63)^ This resulted in Turkish Cypriots withdrawing from the government, and following more intercommunal violence in 1964, a number of Turkish Cypriots moved to the Turkish quarter of Nicosia, causing serious overcrowding.^[\[60\]](#cite_note-64)^{#cite_ref-64}

On 15 July 1974, there was [an attempted coup d'état](/wiki/1974_Cypriot_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "1974 Cypriot coup d'état") led by the [Greek military junta](/wiki/Greek_military_junta_of_1967%E2%80%931974 "Greek military junta of 1967–1974") to unite the island with [Greece](/wiki/Greece "Greece"). The coup ousted president [Makarios III](/wiki/Makarios_III "Makarios III") and replaced him with pro-[enosis](/wiki/Enosis "Enosis") nationalist [Nikos Sampson](/wiki/Nikos_Sampson "Nikos Sampson").^[\[61\]](#cite_note-TIME-65)^{#cite_ref-TIME_65-0}

On 20 July 1974, the [coup d'état](/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "Coup d'état") precipitated the [invasion of the island by the Turkish army](/wiki/Turkish_invasion_of_Cyprus "Turkish invasion of Cyprus").^[\[62\]](#cite_note-66)^ The operation included two phases. The second phase of the Turkish invasion was performed on 14 August 1974, where the Turkish army advanced their positions, eventually capturing a total of 37% of Cypriot territory including the northern part of Nicosia. The fighting left the island with a massive refugee problem on both sides.^[\[63\]](#cite_note-67)^{#cite_ref-67}

On 13 February 1975, the Turkish Cypriot community declared the [Turkish Federated State of Cyprus](/wiki/Turkish_Federated_State_of_Cyprus "Turkish Federated State of Cyprus") in the area occupied by Turkish forces.^[\[64\]](#cite_note-NathanShaw212-68)^ On 15 November 1983, Turkish Cypriots proclaimed their independence as the [Turkish Republic of Northern Cyprus](/wiki/Northern_Cyprus "Northern Cyprus"), that is recognized only by [Turkey](/wiki/Turkey "Turkey") and seen by the international community as a part of the [Republic of Cyprus](/wiki/Cyprus "Cyprus") but not under its effective control.{#cite_ref-NathanShaw212_68-0}

On 23 April 2003, the [Ledra Palace](/wiki/Ledra_Palace "Ledra Palace") crossing was opened through the [Green Line](/wiki/United_Nations_Buffer_Zone_in_Cyprus "United Nations Buffer Zone in Cyprus"), the first time that crossing was allowed since 1974.^[\[65\]](#cite_note-69)^ This was followed by the opening of [Ayios Dometios](/wiki/Ayios_Dometios "Ayios Dometios")/[Metehan](/w/index.php?title=Metehan,_Nicosia&action=edit&redlink=1 "Metehan, Nicosia (page does not exist)") crossing point on 9 May 2003.^[\[66\]](#cite_note-70)^ On 3 April 2008, the [Ledra Street](/wiki/Ledra_Street "Ledra Street") crossing was also reopened.^[\[67\]](#cite_note-71)^{#cite_ref-71}

From 30 October 2016 and onwards, Nicosia became the only capital city in the world that had two [time zones](/wiki/Time_zones "Time zones"), after the parliament of the [de facto](/wiki/De_facto "De facto") Turkish Republic of Northern Cyprus abolished standard time and decided that Northern Cyprus remains at [UTC+03:00](/wiki/UTC%2B03:00 "UTC+03:00") year-round, following Turkey's example.^[\[68\]](#cite_note-72)^^[\[69\]](#cite_note-73)^ The following year, due to criticism from the Turkish Cypriot public in the north, the Turkish Cypriot government decided to go back to standard time, following the rest of Europe.{#cite_ref-73}  

Geography {#Geography}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=9 "Edit section: Geography")\]  

### Climate {#Climate}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=10 "Edit section: Climate")\]

Being in the [rain shadow](/wiki/Rain_shadow "Rain shadow") of the [Troodos Mountains](/wiki/Troodos_Mountains "Troodos Mountains"), Nicosia has a [hot semi-arid climate](/wiki/Hot_semi-arid_climate "Hot semi-arid climate") ([Köppen climate classification](/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification "Köppen climate classification") *BSh* ) due to its low annual precipitation totals and annual temperature range.^[\[70\]](#cite_note-74)^ The city experiences long, hot to sweltering, dry summers, and mild winters, with most of the rainfall occurring in winter. Winter precipitation is occasionally accompanied by [sleet](/wiki/Ice_pellets "Ice pellets") but rarely by [snow](/wiki/Snow "Snow"). The accumulation of snow is particularly rare (last events occurred in 1950, 1974, 1997, 2015 and 2022). There is occasionally light [frost](/wiki/Frost "Frost") during the winter nights. On 4 September 2020, Nicosia recorded a temperature of 46.2 °C (115.2 °F), which is the highest temperature to have ever been recorded in Cyprus.^[\[71\]](#cite_note-75)^{#cite_ref-75}  
{#cite_ref-76}
