Cityscape {#Cityscape}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=11 "Edit section: Cityscape")\]

|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png)](/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg) | This section **needs additional citations for [verification](/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability "Wikipedia:Verifiability")** . Please help [improve this article](/wiki/Special:EditPage/Nicosia "Special:EditPage/Nicosia") by [adding citations to reliable sources](/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners "Help:Referencing for beginners") in this section. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed. *(January 2015)**([Learn how and when to remove this message](/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal "Help:Maintenance template removal"))* |

As of 2023^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit)^, Nicosia holds the unenviable position of being the capital city with the fewest green spaces in Europe, with only three per cent of the city covered with trees.^[\[73\]](#cite_note-77)^{#cite_ref-77}  

### South of the Green Line {#South_of_the_Green_Line}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=12 "Edit section: South of the Green Line")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Nicosia_panoramic_view_Cyprus_Tower_25_Jean_Nouvel.jpg/220px-Nicosia_panoramic_view_Cyprus_Tower_25_Jean_Nouvel.jpg)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_panoramic_view_Cyprus_Tower_25_Jean_Nouvel.jpg) View of Nicosia from [Shacolas Tower](/wiki/Shacolas_Tower "Shacolas Tower") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Nicosia_1.jpg/220px-Nicosia_1.jpg)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_1.jpg) [Ledra Street](/wiki/Ledra_Street "Ledra Street") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Lefkosia-green-line-b.jpg/220px-Lefkosia-green-line-b.jpg)](/wiki/File:Lefkosia-green-line-b.jpg) Buffer zone in Nicosia [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Close_to_the_buffer_zone_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Close_to_the_buffer_zone_-_panoramio.jpg)](/wiki/File:Close_to_the_buffer_zone_-_panoramio.jpg) Street close to the Nicosia border

[Ledra Street](/wiki/Ledra_Street "Ledra Street") is in the middle of the walled city. The street has historically been the busiest shopping street of the capital and adjacent streets lead to the most lively part of the old city with narrow streets, boutiques, bars and art-cafés. The street today is a historic monument on its own, covering about 1 km (0.6 mi) in length and connects the south and north parts of the old city. During the [EOKA struggle](/wiki/EOKA "EOKA") that ran from 1955 to 1959, the street acquired the informal nickname *[The Murder Mile](/wiki/Ledra_Street "Ledra Street")* in reference to the frequent targeting of the British colonialists by nationalist fighters along its course.^[\[74\]](#cite_note-78)^^[\[75\]](#cite_note-79)^ In 1963, during the outbreak of hostilities between the Greek and Turkish Cypriot communities, following the announcement of amendments to the Cypriot Constitution, Turkish Cypriots withdrew to the northern part of Nicosia which became one of the many [Turkish Cypriot enclaves](/wiki/Turkish_Cypriot_enclaves "Turkish Cypriot enclaves") which existed throughout the island. Various streets which ran between the northern and southern part of the city, including Ledra Street, were blockaded. During the Turkish army invasion of Cyprus in 1974, Turkish troops occupied northern Nicosia (as well as the northern part of Cyprus). A buffer zone was established across the island along the ceasefire line to separate the northern Turkish controlled part of the island, and the south. The buffer zone runs through Ledra Street. After many failed attempts on reaching agreement between the two communities, Ledra Street was reopened on 3 April 2008.{#cite_ref-79}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Nicosia_01-2017_img09_StJohn_the_Apostle_Church.jpg/170px-Nicosia_01-2017_img09_StJohn_the_Apostle_Church.jpg)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_01-2017_img09_StJohn_the_Apostle_Church.jpg) [St. John's Cathedral](/wiki/St._John%27s_Cathedral,_Nicosia "St. John's Cathedral, Nicosia")

To the east of Ledra Street, [Faneromeni Square](/wiki/Faneromeni_Square "Faneromeni Square") was the centre of Nicosia before 1974. It hosts a number of historical buildings and monuments including Faneromeni Church, Faneromeni School, Faneromeni Library and the Marble Mausoleum. Faneromeni Church, is a church built in 1872 in the stead of another church located at the same site, constructed with the remains of La Cava castle and a convent. There rest the archbishop and the other bishops who were executed by the Ottomans in the Saray Square during the 1821 revolt. The Palace of the Archbishop can be found at [Archbishop Kyprianos](/wiki/Archbishop_Kyprianos "Archbishop Kyprianos") Square. Although it seems very old, it is a wonderful imitation of typical Venetian style, built in 1956. Next to the palace is the late [Gothic](/wiki/Gothic_architecture "Gothic architecture") [St. John's Cathedral](/wiki/St._John%27s_Cathedral,_Nicosia "St. John's Cathedral, Nicosia") (1665) with picturesque frescos. The square leads to [Onasagorou Street](/wiki/Onasagorou_Street "Onasagorou Street"), another busy shopping street in the historical centre.

The walls surrounding the old city have three gates. In The [Kyrenia Gate](/wiki/Kyrenia_Gate "Kyrenia Gate") which was responsible to the transport to the north, and especially [Kyrenia](/wiki/Kyrenia "Kyrenia"), the [Famagusta Gate](/wiki/Famagusta_Gate "Famagusta Gate") which was responsible for the transport from [Famagusta](/wiki/Famagusta "Famagusta"), [Larnaca](/wiki/Larnaca "Larnaca") and [Limassol](/wiki/Limassol "Limassol") and [Karpasia](/wiki/Karpasia_(town) "Karpasia (town)"), and the [Paphos Gate](/w/index.php?title=Paphos_Gate&action=edit&redlink=1 "Paphos Gate (page does not exist)") for transport to the west and especially [Paphos](/wiki/Paphos "Paphos"). All three gates are well-preserved,^[\[76\]](#cite_note-kesh2-80)^ with Famagusta gate functioning as a venue for art exhibitions and concerts.^[\[77\]](#cite_note-81)^ The historic centre is clearly present inside the walls, but the modern city has grown beyond.{#cite_ref-81}

Presently, the main square of the city is [Eleftheria (Freedom) Square](/wiki/Eleftheria_square "Eleftheria square"), with the city hall, the post office and the library. The square, which has been redesigned by [Zaha Hadid Architects](/wiki/Zaha_Hadid_Architects "Zaha Hadid Architects") and was delivered to the public in 2021,^[\[78\]](#cite_note-82)^ connects the old city with the new city where one can find the main shopping streets such as the prestigious [Stasikratous Street](/wiki/Stasikratous_Street "Stasikratous Street"), [Themistokli Dervi Avenue](/wiki/Themistokli_Dervi_Avenue "Themistokli Dervi Avenue") and [Makariou Avenue](/wiki/Makariou_Avenue,_Nicosia "Makariou Avenue, Nicosia").{#cite_ref-82}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Nicosia_01-2017_img10_Archbishops_Palace.jpg/220px-Nicosia_01-2017_img10_Archbishops_Palace.jpg)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_01-2017_img10_Archbishops_Palace.jpg) Archbishop's Palace

Nicosia is also known for its fine museums. The [Archbishop's Palace](/wiki/Archbishop%27s_Palace,_Nicosia "Archbishop's Palace, Nicosia") contains a [Byzantine](/wiki/Byzantine "Byzantine") museum containing the largest collection of religious icons on the island. [Leventis Municipal Museum](/wiki/Leventio_Museum "Leventio Museum") is the only historical museum of Nicosia and revives the old ways of life in the capital from ancient times up to our days. Other interesting museums include the Folk Art Museum, National Struggle Museum (witnessing the [rebellion against the British administration](/wiki/EOKA "EOKA") in the 1950s), Cyprus Ethnological Museum (House of Dragoman Hadjigeorgakis Kornesios, 18th century) and the Handicrafts centre.

Nicosia also hosts an [Armenian archbishopric](/wiki/Armenian_Diocese_of_Cyprus "Armenian Diocese of Cyprus"), a small Buddhist temple, a [Maronite archbishopric](/wiki/Maronite_Catholic_Archeparchy_of_Cyprus "Maronite Catholic Archeparchy of Cyprus"), and a [Roman Catholic](/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church "Roman Catholic Church") church.  

### North of the Green Line {#North_of_the_Green_Line}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=13 "Edit section: North of the Green Line")\]  
Main article: [North Nicosia § Cityscape](/wiki/North_Nicosia#Cityscape "North Nicosia")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Samanbah%C3%A7e_in_North_Nicosia.jpg/220px-Samanbah%C3%A7e_in_North_Nicosia.jpg)](/wiki/File:Samanbah%C3%A7e_in_North_Nicosia.jpg) The historical Samanbahçe neighborhood [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Nicosia_01-2017_img32_AtatuerkSquare.jpg/170px-Nicosia_01-2017_img32_AtatuerkSquare.jpg)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_01-2017_img32_AtatuerkSquare.jpg) Sarayönü Square [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Night_at_Yeni%C5%9Fehir%2C_Nicosia.jpg/220px-Night_at_Yeni%C5%9Fehir%2C_Nicosia.jpg)](/wiki/File:Night_at_Yeni%C5%9Fehir,_Nicosia.jpg) A view from the [Yenişehir](/wiki/Yeni%C5%9Fehir,_Nicosia "Yenişehir, Nicosia") quarter [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Pedieos_river_walking_routes_Green_leaf_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg/220px-Pedieos_river_walking_routes_Green_leaf_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg)](/wiki/File:Pedieos_river_walking_routes_Green_leaf_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg) Pedieos river walking route

At the centre of the walled city lies the [Sarayönü Square](/wiki/Saray%C3%B6n%C3%BC_Square "Sarayönü Square"). The square has been dubbed as "the heart of Nicosia" and historically has been the cultural centre of the Turkish Cypriot community.^[\[79\]](#cite_note-sarac-83)^ In the middle of the square stands the Venetian Column, known simply as "the Obelisk" ("Dikiltaş") to the locals and symbolic of the country's government.^[\[79\]](#cite_note-sarac-83)^ The column was brought from the ancient city of [Salamis](/wiki/Salamis,_Cyprus "Salamis, Cyprus") by the Venetians in 1550.^[\[80\]](#cite_note-84)^ The Girne Avenue connects Sarayönü to the [Kyrenia Gate](/wiki/Kyrenia_Gate "Kyrenia Gate") and the İnönü Square in front of it. The avenue has been described as "the symbol of the walled city", and is filled with numerous shops and restaurants.^[\[81\]](#cite_note-85)^{#cite_ref-85}

Next to the [Ledra Street](/wiki/Ledra_Street "Ledra Street") checkpoint is the [Arasta](/w/index.php?title=Arasta&action=edit&redlink=1 "Arasta (page does not exist)") area. The area was pedestrianized in 2013 and is home to a network of historic shopping streets, reflecting an eastern shopping tradition with food and traditional items.^[\[82\]](#cite_note-86)^ Nearby [Büyük Han](/wiki/B%C3%BCy%C3%BCk_Han "Büyük Han"), the largest caravanserai in the island and considered to be one of the finest buildings in Cyprus, was built in 1572 by the [Ottomans](/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire") and functions as a cultural centre.^[\[83\]](#cite_note-87)^^[\[84\]](#cite_note-88)^ To the west of the Girne Avenue lies the Samanbahçe neighborhood, built in the 19th century by the government, considered to be the first example of social housing in the island. Still a residential area, the neighborhood is considered to be one of the best representations of the Cypriot culture.^[\[85\]](#cite_note-89)^ Another central point in the walled city is the [Selimiye Mosque](/wiki/Selimiye_Mosque,_Nicosia "Selimiye Mosque, Nicosia"), originally built as the St. Sophia Cathedral. The mosque is the chief religious centre in Northern Cyprus. It was built between 1209 and 1228 by the Latin Church of Cyprus, in a Gothic style resembling French cathedrals.^[\[86\]](#cite_note-90)^ Next to the mosque is the [Bedesten](/wiki/Bedesten "Bedesten"), a large Greek church in the Byzantine and Gothic styles, built in the 14th century. It was used as a marketplace in the Ottoman era. Today, it is used as a cultural centre where various cultural activities such as concerts and festivals take place.^[\[87\]](#cite_note-91)^^[\[88\]](#cite_note-stwingcity-92)^{#cite_ref-stwingcity_92-0}

The quarters of Nicosia outside the walled city are more spacious than the walled city, with wider roads and junctions. These areas are characterized by multi-floor concrete buildings. In the outskirts of the city, a number large and imposing villas have been built that belong to the middle and upper-classes.^[\[89\]](#cite_note-93)^ The [Dereboyu Avenue](/wiki/Dereboyu_Avenue "Dereboyu Avenue") serves as the modern heart of the northern part and is its centre of entertainment.{#cite_ref-93}  

Politics and administration {#Politics_and_administration}
----------------------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=14 "Edit section: Politics and administration")\]  

### Governance of the metropolitan area {#Governance_of_the_metropolitan_area}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=15 "Edit section: Governance of the metropolitan area")\]
[![Map of Greater Nicosia](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/48/Nicosia_conurbation_map.png/250px-Nicosia_conurbation_map.png)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_conurbation_map.png) Greater Nicosia

Greater Nicosia is administered by several municipalities. In the centre is the city municipality of Nicosia itself (see below). Other municipalities are [Strovolos](/wiki/Strovolos "Strovolos"), [Lakatamia](/wiki/Lakatamia "Lakatamia"), [Latsia](/wiki/Latsia "Latsia"), [Aglandjia](/wiki/Aglandjia "Aglandjia"), [Engomi](/wiki/Engomi "Engomi"), [Agios Dhometios](/wiki/Agios_Dhometios "Agios Dhometios") and the newly formed (as of 2011^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit)^) [Yeri](/wiki/Yeri,_Cyprus "Yeri, Cyprus") \& [Tseri](/wiki/Tseri "Tseri").

The population of the conurbation is 300,000 (2011 census, plus Turkish Cypriot administered census of 2006) of which 100,000 live within the Nicosia municipal area. Because Nicosia municipality has separate communal municipal administrations, the population of Strovolos (67,904 (2011 Census)) is actually the largest of all the local authorities in Greater Nicosia.

Within Nicosia municipality, most of the population resides in the more recently annexed outlying areas of [Kaimakli](/wiki/Kaimakli "Kaimakli"), [Pallouriotissa](/wiki/Pallouriotissa "Pallouriotissa"), [Omorfita](/wiki/Omorfita "Omorfita") and [Ayii Omoloyites](/wiki/Ayioi_Omoloyites,_Nicosia "Ayioi Omoloyites, Nicosia").

There is no metropolitan authority as such for Greater Nicosia and various roles, responsibilities and functions for the wider area are undertaken by the Nicosia District administration, bodies such as the Nicosia Water Board and, to some extent, Nicosia municipality.

The Nicosia Water Board supplies water to the following municipalities: Nicosia, Strovolos, Aglandjia, Engomi, Ay. Dometios, Latsia, Geri and Tseri. The board consists of three persons nominated by the Council of each municipality, plus three members appointed by the government, who are usually the District Officer of Nicosia District, who chairs the Board, the Accountant General and the Director of the Water Department. The board also supply Anthoupolis and Ergates, for whom the government provide representatives. Thus the board is in the majority controlled by the municipalities of Greater Nicosia in providing this vital local government service.^[\[90\]](#cite_note-94)^{#cite_ref-94}

The Nicosia Sewerage Board, is likewise majority controlled by the municipalities of Greater Nicosia. It is chaired *ex officio* by the Mayor of Nicosia and consists of members chosen by the municipalities of Nicosia (6 members), Strovolos (5 members), Aglandjia (2 members), Lakatamia (2 members), Ay. Dometios (2 members), Engomi (2 members), Latsia (1 member). The sewage treatment plant is at [Mia Milia](/wiki/Mia_Milia "Mia Milia"). The Nicosia Sewerage System serves a population of approximately 140,000 and an area of 20 km^2^ (8 sq mi). Approximately 30% of the influent is contributed by the Turkish Cypriot Side.^[\[91\]](#cite_note-95)^{#cite_ref-95}

Public transport is not controlled by the local authorities, but comes under the Nicosia District administration, which is an arm of the Ministry of the Interior. Transport services (primarily bus and taxi) are provided by private operators such as OSEL.^[\[92\]](#cite_note-96)^ In late 2019 the contract for providing transport services in the district of Nicosia was awarded via tender to a private consortium which was expected to take over the system on 5 July 2020.^[\[93\]](#cite_note-97)^^[\[94\]](#cite_note-98)^{#cite_ref-98}  

### Nicosia Municipality {#Nicosia_Municipality}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=16 "Edit section: Nicosia Municipality")\]  
See also: [List of mayors of Nicosia Municipality](/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Nicosia_Municipality "List of mayors of Nicosia Municipality")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/NICOSIA%2C_11_AUGUST%2C_2011_114.jpg/170px-NICOSIA%2C_11_AUGUST%2C_2011_114.jpg)](/wiki/File:NICOSIA,_11_AUGUST,_2011_114.jpg) The old building of the Nicosia Municipality at [Eleftheria Square](/wiki/Eleftheria_square "Eleftheria square")

The [Nicosia Municipality](/wiki/Nicosia_Municipality "Nicosia Municipality") is responsible for all the municipal duties within the walled city and the immediately adjacent areas. The Constitution states that various main government buildings and headquarters must be situated within the Nicosia municipal boundaries.^[\[95\]](#cite_note-99)^ However separate municipalities are prescribed by the constitution for in the five largest towns, including Nicosia,^[\[96\]](#cite_note-100)^ and in the case of Nicosia the separate administration was established in 1958. The Turkish Municipal Committees (Temporary Provisions) Law, 1959^[\[97\]](#cite_note-101)^ established a municipal authority run by a "Turkish Municipal Committee", defined as "the body of persons set up on or after the first day of July, 1958, in the towns of Nicosia, Limassol, Famagusta, Larnaca and Paphos by the Turkish inhabitants thereof for the purpose of performing municipal functions within the municipal limits of such towns".The "[Nicosia Turkish Municipality](/wiki/Nicosia_Turkish_Municipality "Nicosia Turkish Municipality")", founded in 1958, carries out municipal duties in the northern and north-western part of city.^[\[98\]](#cite_note-102)^ The remaining areas, in the south and east of the city, are administered by [Nicosia Municipality](/wiki/Nicosia_Municipality "Nicosia Municipality").{#cite_ref-102}  

### Nicosia Turkish Municipality {#Nicosia_Turkish_Municipality}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: Nicosia Turkish Municipality")\]
[![Nicosia Turkish Municipal building](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Lefko%C5%9Fa_T%C3%BCrk_Belediyesi.JPG/220px-Lefko%C5%9Fa_T%C3%BCrk_Belediyesi.JPG)](/wiki/File:Lefko%C5%9Fa_T%C3%BCrk_Belediyesi.JPG) Nicosia Turkish Municipal building

The first attempt to establish a [Nicosia Turkish Municipality](/wiki/Nicosia_Turkish_Municipality "Nicosia Turkish Municipality") was made in 1958. In October 1959, the British Colonial Administration passed the Turkish Municipality Committees law. In 1960 with the declaration of independence of Cyprus, the Constitution of the [Republic of Cyprus](/wiki/Republic_of_Cyprus "Republic of Cyprus") gave Turkish Cypriots the right to establish their own municipality.^[\[99\]](#cite_note-103)^^[\[100\]](#cite_note-104)^^[\[101\]](#cite_note-const-105)^ As negotiations between the two sides to establish separate municipalities failed in 1962, implementing legislation was never passed.^[\[102\]](#cite_note-106)^^[\[103\]](#cite_note-107)^ Since the complete division of Nicosia following the Turkish Invasion in 1974, the [Nicosia Turkish Municipality](/wiki/Nicosia_Turkish_Municipality "Nicosia Turkish Municipality") has become the [de facto](/wiki/De_facto "De facto") local authority of northern Nicosia. The [Nicosia Turkish Municipality](/wiki/Nicosia_Turkish_Municipality "Nicosia Turkish Municipality") is a member of the Union of Cyprus Turkish Municipalities.^[\[104\]](#cite_note-108)^ The mayor is [Mehmet Harmancı](/wiki/Mehmet_Harmanc%C4%B1 "Mehmet Harmancı") from the [Communal Democracy Party](/wiki/Communal_Democracy_Party "Communal Democracy Party").{#cite_ref-108}  

### Other municipalities in Greater Nicosia {#Other_municipalities_in_Greater_Nicosia}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: Other municipalities in Greater Nicosia")\]

Until 1986 there were no suburban municipalities. Then, following the procedures in the Municipal Law 111/1985, Strovolos, Engomi, Ay. Dometios, Aglandjia, Latsia and Lakatamia were erected into municipalities.^[\[105\]](#cite_note-109)^ Each municipal council has the number of members described in the Municipal Law 111/1985 depending on the population figures. All members of the council are elected directly by the people for a period of 5 years.{#cite_ref-109}  

### Administrative divisions and demographics {#Administrative_divisions_and_demographics}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: Administrative divisions and demographics")\]  
Main article: [Administrative divisions of Nicosia](/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Nicosia "Administrative divisions of Nicosia")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Nicosia_local_government_units_%282%29.png/220px-Nicosia_local_government_units_%282%29.png)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_local_government_units_(2).png) Administrative divisions (2011 Census)

Nicosia within the city limits is divided into 29 administrative units, according to the latest census. This unit is termed in English as *[quarter](/wiki/Quarter_(urban_subdivision) "Quarter (urban subdivision)"), neighborhood, [parish](/wiki/Parish "Parish"), enoria* or *[mahalla](/wiki/Mahalla "Mahalla")* . These units are: [Ayios Andreas](/wiki/Ayios_Andreas,_Nicosia "Ayios Andreas, Nicosia") (formerly Tophane), [Trypiotis](/wiki/Trypiotis "Trypiotis"), [Nebethane](/wiki/Nebethane,_Nicosia "Nebethane, Nicosia"), [Tabakhane](/wiki/Tabakhane,_Nicosia "Tabakhane, Nicosia"), Phaneromeni, [Ayios Savvas](/wiki/Ayios_Savvas,_Nicosia "Ayios Savvas, Nicosia"), Omerie, [Ayios Antonios](/wiki/Ayios_Antonios,_Nicosia "Ayios Antonios, Nicosia") (St. Anthony), St. John, [Taht-el-kale](/wiki/Taht-el-kale,_Nicosia "Taht-el-kale, Nicosia"), Chrysaliniotissa, [Ayios Kassianos (Kafesli)](/wiki/Ayios_Kassianos,_Nicosia "Ayios Kassianos, Nicosia"), [Kaïmakli](/wiki/Kaimakli "Kaimakli"), [Panayia, St Constantine \& Helen](/wiki/Pallouriotissa "Pallouriotissa"), [Ayioi Omoloyites](/wiki/Ayioi_Omoloyites,_Nicosia "Ayioi Omoloyites, Nicosia"), [Arab Ahmet](/wiki/Arab_Ahmet,_Nicosia "Arab Ahmet, Nicosia"), [Yeni Jami](/wiki/Yeni_Jami,_Nicosia "Yeni Jami, Nicosia"), [Omorfita](/wiki/Omorfita "Omorfita"), Ibrahim Pasha, Mahmut Pasha, [Abu Kavouk](/wiki/Ak_Kavuk,_Nicosia "Ak Kavuk, Nicosia"), [St. Luke](/wiki/Ayios_Loukas,_Nicosia "Ayios Loukas, Nicosia"), Abdi Chavush, [Iplik Pazar and Korkut Effendi](/wiki/Iplik_Pazar_and_Korkut_Effendi "Iplik Pazar and Korkut Effendi"), Ayia Sophia, [Haydar Pasha](/wiki/Haydar_Pasha,_Nicosia "Haydar Pasha, Nicosia"), Karamanzade,^[\[106\]](#cite_note-110)^ and [Yenişehir/Neapolis](/wiki/Yeni%C5%9Fehir,_Nicosia "Yenişehir, Nicosia").^[\[107\]](#cite_note-Neapoli_quarter-111)^{#cite_ref-Neapoli_quarter_111-0}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Parlanet_cyprus.jpg/220px-Parlanet_cyprus.jpg)](/wiki/File:Parlanet_cyprus.jpg) Presidential Palace in Strovolos area.

The municipality of Strovolos, established in 1986, is the second largest municipal authority in Cyprus in terms of population after Limassol and encompasses the southern suburbs of the capital immediately adjacent to Nicosia municipality.^[\[108\]](#cite_note-112)^ [Lakatamia](/wiki/Lakatamia "Lakatamia"), [Latsia](/wiki/Latsia "Latsia"), [Geri](/wiki/Geri,_Cyprus "Geri, Cyprus") and [Aglandjia](/wiki/Aglandjia "Aglandjia") are other separate municipalities in the Nicosia metropolitan area.{#cite_ref-112}

The town of [Gönyeli](/wiki/G%C3%B6nyeli "Gönyeli") is now conurbated with the northern suburbs. Previously a village authority, it now functions as a municipality^[\[109\]](#cite_note-113)^ within the same area^[\[110\]](#cite_note-114)^ The suburbs immediately to the north of the city have not organized into municipalities. The village authority of [Hamitköy](/wiki/Hamitk%C3%B6y "Hamitköy") (also known as Hamid Mandres) is highly urbanized^[\[111\]](#cite_note-115)^ and was included within the borders of Nicosia Turkish Municipality^[\[112\]](#cite_note-116)^ as a Nicosia neighborhood headed by a [muhtar](/wiki/Muhtar_(title) "Muhtar (title)").^[\[113\]](#cite_note-117)^ [Ortakeuy](/wiki/Ortakioi "Ortakioi") Village authority^[\[114\]](#cite_note-118)^ has similarly been redefined as a neighborhood of Nicosia Turkish Municipality.{#cite_ref-118}  

Demographics {#Demographics}
----------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Demographics")\]  

### Religion {#Religion}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Religion")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Nicosia_01-2017_img18_View_from_Shacolas_Tower.jpg/220px-Nicosia_01-2017_img18_View_from_Shacolas_Tower.jpg)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_01-2017_img18_View_from_Shacolas_Tower.jpg) Holy Cross Church

Historically Nicosia is a melting pot harmonizing multiple religious establishments, denominations, churches, mosques, synagogues, etc. Traditionally Nicosia hosts Greek Orthodox churches, Armenian Apostolic churches, Latin Catholic, Maronite Catholic, Anglican churches, Evangelical churches as well as mosques and synagogues.  

#### Armenian Apostolic Church {#Armenian_Apostolic_Church}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Armenian Apostolic Church")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Sourp_Asdvadzadzin-front.jpg/170px-Sourp_Asdvadzadzin-front.jpg)](/wiki/File:Sourp_Asdvadzadzin-front.jpg) Armenian Apostolic Church in Nicosia

One of the oldest Armenian churches known as the Benedictine Abbey of Our Lady of Tyre, was founded in the 13th century as a principal convent following the fall of Jerusalem. In 1308, the Lusignan king, [Henry II of Jerusalem](/wiki/Henry_II_of_Jerusalem "Henry II of Jerusalem"), repaired the church after it was destroyed by an earthquake. As many of the nuns were Armenian in origin, it came under the Armenian Church before 1504.^[\[115\]](#cite_note-Hadjilyras-1-119)^ Since 1963, the church has been located in [North Nicosia](/wiki/North_Nicosia "North Nicosia"), under Turkish Cypriot administration. The church suffered the collapse of some parts and a great deterioration of condition till 2007, when the restoration work began.^[\[116\]](#cite_note-undpbooklet-120)^ The renovation was completed in 2013^[\[117\]](#cite_note-121)^ and won the EU Prize For Cultural Heritage (Europa Nostra Award) in 2015.^[\[118\]](#cite_note-122)^ With the help of the World Council of Churches, the Church of Westphalia, the Cyprus government and the faithful, a new church was built in Strovolos, also called "Sourp Asdvadzadzin". Its foundation stone was laid on 25 September 1976 by Archbishop Makarios III and Archbishop Nerses Pakhdigian. It was officially inaugurated on 22 November 1981 by Catholicos of Cilicia Khoren I and Coadjutor Catholicos of Cilicia Karekin II, in the presence of Archbishop Chrysostomos I, Bishop Zareh Aznavorian and Representative Dr. Antranik L. Ashdjian.{#cite_ref-122}  

#### Maronite Catholic Church {#Maronite_Catholic_Church}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: Maronite Catholic Church")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Nicosia_by_Paride_11.JPG/170px-Nicosia_by_Paride_11.JPG)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_by_Paride_11.JPG) Maronite Church in Nicosia

The Maronite community is a traditional community in Nicosia. The archeparchy extends its jurisdiction over all the faithful Maronites of the island of Cyprus. Its arcieparchial seat is the city of Nicosia, where is located the [Our Lady of Grace Cathedral (Nicosia)](/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Grace_Cathedral_(Nicosia) "Our Lady of Grace Cathedral (Nicosia)").

The archeparchy at the end of 2013 out of a population of 838,897 people had 10,400 baptized, corresponding to 1.2% of the total. Its territory is divided into 12 parishes. *Our Lady of Grace Cathedral* is the main Maronite church of the city of Nicosia, in Cyprus, and is the cathedral of the [Maronite Catholic Archeparchy of Cyprus](/wiki/Maronite_Catholic_Archeparchy_of_Cyprus "Maronite Catholic Archeparchy of Cyprus").

The first cathedral was dedicated to St. John, but during the Ottoman occupation it was turned into a mosque. The Lebanese Maronite community erected the church of Santa Croce, later entrusted to the Franciscans, and the current church of Our Lady of Grace is near to the Franciscan church. In 1960, the seat of the vicarage and the surrounding buildings were built.^[\[119\]](#cite_note-123)^ On 6 June 2010 [Pope Benedict XVI](/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI "Pope Benedict XVI"), the first pope to make an apostolic trip to the island, visited the cathedral of Nicosia.^[\[120\]](#cite_note-124)^{#cite_ref-124}  

#### Anglican Church {#Anglican_Church}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Anglican Church")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/St-Pauls-Cathedral-Nicosia.jpg/170px-St-Pauls-Cathedral-Nicosia.jpg)](/wiki/File:St-Pauls-Cathedral-Nicosia.jpg) Anglican Church in Nicosia

The church of St. Paul was built in 1893 when Cyprus was a protectorate of the British Empire. The influence of politics on architecture is evident by the structural elements of the building, which is reminiscent of an English parish church. The Christian church today is part of the Diocese of Cyprus and the Gulf.  

#### Greek Evangelical Church {#Greek_Evangelical_Church}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Greek Evangelical Church")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Greek_Evangelical_Church_Nicosia.jpg/220px-Greek_Evangelical_Church_Nicosia.jpg)](/wiki/File:Greek_Evangelical_Church_Nicosia.jpg) Greek Evangelical Church of Nicosia

The Greek Evangelical Church of Nicosia is a relatively modern architecture serving the local Protestant community. Along with special hours dedicated to services of the Greek Evangelical community, it serves as a worship centre of local Protestants of other nationalities, such as Armenian, American, Romanian, Korean, Chinese, etc. It is located on Gladstone Street.^[\[121\]](#cite_note-125)^{#cite_ref-125}  

#### Armenian Evangelical Church {#Armenian_Evangelical_Church}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Armenian Evangelical Church")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Nicosia_Armenian_Evangelical.jpg/220px-Nicosia_Armenian_Evangelical.jpg)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_Armenian_Evangelical.jpg) Armenian Evangelical Church of Nicosia

The first [Armenian Evangelicals](/wiki/Armenian_Evangelical_Church "Armenian Evangelical Church") in Cyprus came after the arrival of the [British](/wiki/United_Kingdom "United Kingdom") in July 1878. As they were not committed, and very few in number, they quickly became associated with the *Mother Church* ([Armenian Apostolic Church](/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church "Armenian Apostolic Church")), such as Apisoghom Utidjian, the official state documents translator and the son of Stepan Utidjian, one of the original founders of the [Armenian Evangelical Church](/wiki/Armenian_Evangelical_Church "Armenian Evangelical Church"), who served as chairman of the Nicosia parish council for 30 years. With the influx of more [Protestants](/wiki/Protestants "Protestants"), [Armenian Evangelicals](/wiki/Armenian_Evangelical_Church "Armenian Evangelical Church") became affiliated with the [Reformed Presbyterian Church](/wiki/Reformed_Presbyterian_Church_of_North_America "Reformed Presbyterian Church of North America") as early as 1887. Although the main centres were Nicosia and [Larnaca](/wiki/Larnaca "Larnaca"), gatherings were occasionally held in [Limassol](/wiki/Limassol "Limassol"), [Famagusta](/wiki/Famagusta "Famagusta"), and [Amiandos](/wiki/Pano_Amiantos "Pano Amiantos").

There was also a small Armenian Evangelical church, located on Mahmoud Pasha Street, in the Turkish-occupied part of the walled city of Nicosia---behind the old American Academy building, near the [Arab Ahmed mosque](/wiki/Arabahmet_Mosque "Arabahmet Mosque"). Prior to its erection, [Armenian Evangelicals](/wiki/Armenian_Evangelical_Church "Armenian Evangelical Church") used to worship God at the Reformed Presbyterian Church on Apostolos Varnavas Street, opposite the old Powerhouse and behind the building of the Holy Archbishopric of Cyprus. The church - a vision already since the early 1930s - was eventually built thanks to the initiative of pastor Yohanna Der Megerditchian, with the financial contribution of the [Reformed Presbyterian Church](/wiki/Reformed_Presbyterian_Church_of_North_America "Reformed Presbyterian Church of North America") and the Armenian Evangelical faithful; its architect was Dickran H. Davidian. Its foundation stone was laid on 28 July 1946 by pastor Yohanna Der Megerditchian, who dedicated it on 1 July 1947. On the lower part of the right wall to the side of the entrance, there is an inscription in [Armenian](/wiki/Armenian_language "Armenian language").  

#### Converted cathedral {#Converted_cathedral}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Converted cathedral")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Nicosia_church.jpg/220px-Nicosia_church.jpg)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_church.jpg) [Selimiye Mosque](/wiki/Selimiye_Mosque,_Nicosia "Selimiye Mosque, Nicosia"), converted from a cathedral as the right of conquest

Perhaps the most iconic religious architecture of Nicosia is the Cathedral of Saint Sophia, also known as the Agia Sophia of Nicosia, which was constructed in the year of 1326 as a Catholic church. It was converted into a [mosque](/wiki/Mosque "Mosque") and it is located in North Nicosia. It has historically been the main mosque of the city. As a mosque it is known as the Selimiye Mosque which is housed in the largest and oldest surviving [Gothic](/wiki/Gothic_architecture "Gothic architecture") church in [Cyprus](/wiki/Cyprus "Cyprus") (interior dimensions: 66 m × 21 m or 217 by 69 feet) possibly constructed on the site of an earlier [Byzantine](/wiki/Byzantine "Byzantine") church.^[\[122\]](#cite_note-126)^ During the 50-day [Ottoman](/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire") [siege of the city in 1570](/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Venetian_War_(1570%E2%80%931573) "Ottoman–Venetian War (1570–1573)"), the cathedral provided refuge for a great number of people. When the city fell on 9 September, Francesco Contarini, the Bishop of Paphos, delivered the last Christian sermon in the building, in which he asked for divine help and exhorted the people. The cathedral was stormed by Ottoman soldiers, who broke the door and killed the bishop along with others. They smashed or threw out Christian items, such as furniture and ornaments in the cathedral^[\[123\]](#cite_note-kesh-127)^ and destroyed the choir as well as the nave.^[\[124\]](#cite_note-gurkan-128)^ Then, they washed the interior of the mosque to make it ready for the first [Friday prayer](/wiki/Friday_prayer "Friday prayer") that it would host on 15 September, which was attended by the commander [Lala Mustafa Pasha](/wiki/Lala_Mustafa_Pasha "Lala Mustafa Pasha") and saw the official conversion of the cathedral into a mosque.^[\[123\]](#cite_note-kesh-127)^ According to [Islamic jurisprudence](/wiki/Fiqh "Fiqh"), the main temple of a city conquered by Muslims and not surrendered in peace may be converted to a mosque as a symbol of the takeover and superiority of Islam. This is referred to as "the right of the sword".^[\[125\]](#cite_note-129)^ During the same year, the two [minarets](/wiki/Minaret "Minaret") were added, as well as Islamic features such as the [mihrab](/wiki/Mihrab "Mihrab") (prayer niche) and the [minbar](/wiki/Minbar "Minbar") (sermon pulpit).^[\[126\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAlasya2002363-130)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAlasya2002363_130-0}

The first [imam](/wiki/Imam "Imam") of the mosque was Moravizade Ahmet Efendi, who hailed from the [Morea](/wiki/Morea "Morea") province of the Ottoman Empire.^[\[127\]](#cite_note-131)^ All imams maintained the tradition of climbing the stairs to the minbar before Friday sermons while leaning on a sword used during the conquest of Nicosia to signify that Nicosia was captured by conquest.^[\[128\]](#cite_note-132)^{#cite_ref-132}

Following its conversion, the mosque became the property of the Sultan Selim Foundation, which was responsible for maintaining it. Other donors formed a number of foundations to help with the maintenance.^[\[129\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBağışkan2013-133)^ Okçuzade Mehmed Paşa, a governor of Cyprus in the 16th century, donated a shop to provide income for the Sultan Selim Foundation; other donations include estates in the countryside and other shops. The foundation employed trustees (*mütevelli* ) to look after the funds and transferred 40,000 *[akçe](/wiki/Ak%C3%A7e "Akçe")* annually to [Medina](/wiki/Medina "Medina") in late 16th century.^[\[130\]](#cite_note-134)^ During the Ottoman period, it was the largest mosque in the whole island, and was used weekly by the Ottoman governor, administrators and elite for the Friday prayers. In the late 18th century, a large procession that consisted of the leading officials in the front on horseback, followed by lower-ranking officials on foot, came to the mosque every Friday.^[\[129\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBağışkan2013-133)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBağışkan2013_133-1}  

#### Islam {#Islam}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Islam")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Nicosia_01-2017_img13_Omeriye_Mosque.jpg/220px-Nicosia_01-2017_img13_Omeriye_Mosque.jpg)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_01-2017_img13_Omeriye_Mosque.jpg) Omeriye Mosque in Nicosia

Historically Nicosia (south and north) hosts over 15 mosques, either originally constructed as such or converted from a church. The Ömeriye Mosque, formerly known as the Augustinian Church of Saint Mary is a mosque in the walled city of Nicosia on the island of [Cyprus](/wiki/Cyprus "Cyprus"), currently located in the south section of Nicosia.^[\[131\]](#cite_note-TDV-135)^ Following the [Turkish invasion of Cyprus](/wiki/Turkish_invasion_of_Cyprus "Turkish invasion of Cyprus"), the mosque gained significance as one of the most important sites of Muslim worship in the non-Muslim section of the island and the city.^[\[131\]](#cite_note-TDV-135)^ Currently, the mosque is functioning and open for both worshippers and visitors.^[\[132\]](#cite_note-History_Köseoğlu-136)^^[\[133\]](#cite_note-Vesna_Maric-137)^{#cite_ref-Vesna_Maric_137-0}

Formerly, the site of the mosque was occupied by the Augustinian Church of Saint Mary, which dated back to the 14th century. During the [Ottoman-Venetian War of 1570-73](/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Venetian_War_(1570%E2%80%9373) "Ottoman–Venetian War (1570–73)"), the church was first heavily damaged during the [siege of Nicosia](/wiki/Siege_of_Nicosia "Siege of Nicosia") in 1570, and was eventually levelled after the war.^[\[132\]](#cite_note-History_Köseoğlu-136)^{#cite_ref-History_Köseoğlu_136-1}

After the Turkish conquest of Cyprus, [Lala Mustafa Pasha](/wiki/Lala_Mustafa_Pasha "Lala Mustafa Pasha"), the Ottoman commander, ordered a mosque to be built on the site of the former church,^[\[132\]](#cite_note-History_Köseoğlu-136)^ based on a popular belief that [Umar](/wiki/Umar "Umar"), second [caliph](/wiki/Caliph "Caliph") of Islam, was buried at this site in 7th century.^[\[133\]](#cite_note-Vesna_Maric-137)^{#cite_ref-Vesna_Maric_137-1}

According to [Turkish Cypriot](/wiki/Turkish_Cypriot "Turkish Cypriot") folklore, the Ömeriye Mosque is the first mosque where [Turks](/wiki/Turkish_people "Turkish people") prayed on the island following its conquest in 1571.^[\[134\]](#cite_note-Haber7-138)^{#cite_ref-Haber7_138-0}  

Culture {#Culture}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Culture")\]
[![Photo of Cyprus Archeological Museum in Nicosia](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Nicosia_01-2017_img28_Cyprus_Museum.jpg/220px-Nicosia_01-2017_img28_Cyprus_Museum.jpg)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_01-2017_img28_Cyprus_Museum.jpg) [Cypriot Archeological Museum](/wiki/Cyprus_Museum "Cyprus Museum") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Leventis_Gallery%2C_Nicosia%2C_Cyprus._Adamantios_Diamantis_-_The_World_of_Cyprus-1.jpg/220px-Leventis_Gallery%2C_Nicosia%2C_Cyprus._Adamantios_Diamantis_-_The_World_of_Cyprus-1.jpg)](/wiki/File:Leventis_Gallery,_Nicosia,_Cyprus._Adamantios_Diamantis_-_The_World_of_Cyprus-1.jpg) *The World of Cyprus* , an acrylic painting with a total length of 17.5 meters by Adamantios Diamantis in [Leventis Gallery](/wiki/Leventis_Gallery "Leventis Gallery")

The [Cyprus Museum](/wiki/Cyprus_Museum "Cyprus Museum") is the largest and oldest archaeological museum in Cyprus. In old Nicosia, the Ethnological Museum ([Hadjigeorgakis Kornesios Mansion](/wiki/Hadjigeorgakis_Kornesios_Mansion "Hadjigeorgakis Kornesios Mansion")) is the most important example of surviving urban architecture of the late Ottoman rule. Today, the mansion which was awarded the [Europa Nostra](/wiki/Europa_Nostra "Europa Nostra") prize for its exemplary renovation work, functions as a museum where a collection of artifacts from the Byzantine, Medieval and Ottoman periods are displayed. Other museums in Nicosia include the [Cyprus Museum of Natural History](/wiki/Cyprus_Museum_of_Natural_History "Cyprus Museum of Natural History") and the [Leventis Municipal Museum of Nicosia](/wiki/Leventis_Municipal_Museum_of_Nicosia "Leventis Municipal Museum of Nicosia") and Von World Pens Hall in the south. In the north, the [Dervish Pasha Mansion](/wiki/Dervish_Pasha_Mansion "Dervish Pasha Mansion"), similar in architecture to the Hadjigeorgakis Kornesios Mansion, serves as an ethnological museum, displaying Ottoman and archaeological artifacts.^[\[135\]](#cite_note-139)^ Other museums include the [Lusignan House](/wiki/Lusignan_House "Lusignan House"),^[\[136\]](#cite_note-140)^ the [Mevlevi Tekke Museum](/wiki/Mevlevi_Tekke_Museum "Mevlevi Tekke Museum"), associated with the sect of the [Whirling Dervishes](/wiki/Whirling_Dervishes "Whirling Dervishes"),^[\[137\]](#cite_note-141)^ and the Lapidary Museum.^[\[138\]](#cite_note-142)^{#cite_ref-142}

Art galleries in Nicosia include the [Leventis Gallery](/wiki/Leventis_Gallery "Leventis Gallery"), which hosts over 800 paintings from Cypriot, Greek or European artists.

Nicosia offers a wide variety of musical and theatrical events, organized either by the municipality or independent organizations. Halls and theaters used for this purpose include:

* The Cyprus National Theater, which contains two performance spaces:^[\[139\]](#cite_note-143)^
  * the 550-seat Lyric Theater with a bold exterior but an intimate theatrical environment. Its design minimizes the distance from actor to audience;
  * the 150-seat New Theater, which is an open-ended workshop space, with simple galleries around the room. The stage can be set in the centre, at the ends, or to one side of the room, and the space can be opened to the private garden beyond.
  {#cite_ref-143}
* The Pallas Cinema-Theater which was renovated from a near derelict state in 2008.^[\[140\]](#cite_note-144)^{#cite_ref-144}
* Theatro Ena^[\[141\]](#cite_note-145)^{#cite_ref-145}
* Maskarini Theater^[\[142\]](#cite_note-146)^^[\[143\]](#cite_note-147)^{#cite_ref-147}
* Dionysos Theater^[\[144\]](#cite_note-148)^^[\[145\]](#cite_note-149)^{#cite_ref-149}
* Melina Mercouri Hall^[\[146\]](#cite_note-150)^{#cite_ref-150}
* Theatro Dentro

Nicosia's universities also boast an array of facilities, and many churches and outdoor spaces are used to host cultural events.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ The Near East University hosts the Atatürk Cultural and Conference centre, with 700 seats.^[\[147\]](#cite_note-151)^{#cite_ref-151}

Nicosia hosted the [Miss Universe 2000](/wiki/Miss_Universe_2000 "Miss Universe 2000") pageant.^[\[148\]](#cite_note-152)^{#cite_ref-152}

In June 2011, Nicosia launched a failed campaign to become the [European Capital of Culture](/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture "European Capital of Culture") for 2017.^[\[149\]](#cite_note-153)^{#cite_ref-153}  

Human resources {#Human_resources}
----------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Human resources")\]  

### Education {#Education}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Education")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Panoramic_view_University_of_Cyprus_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg/220px-Panoramic_view_University_of_Cyprus_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg)](/wiki/File:Panoramic_view_University_of_Cyprus_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg) Section of the modern buildings of the [University of Cyprus](/wiki/University_of_Cyprus "University of Cyprus") (UCY) [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Melkonian_entrance.JPG/170px-Melkonian_entrance.JPG)](/wiki/File:Melkonian_entrance.JPG) An entrance to the [Melkonian Educational Institute](/wiki/Melkonian_Educational_Institute "Melkonian Educational Institute")

Nicosia has a large student community as it is the seat of five universities, the [University of Cyprus](/wiki/University_of_Cyprus "University of Cyprus") (UCY), the [University of Nicosia](/wiki/University_of_Nicosia "University of Nicosia"), the [European University Cyprus](/wiki/European_University_Cyprus "European University Cyprus"), the [Open University of Cyprus](/wiki/Open_University_of_Cyprus "Open University of Cyprus") and [Frederick University](/wiki/Frederick_University "Frederick University"). In addition, the city is home to the oldest still-operational [high-school](/wiki/Lyceum "Lyceum") in Cyprus, [Pancyprian Gymnasium](/wiki/Pancyprian_Gymnasium "Pancyprian Gymnasium").

Nicosia is also home to one of the largest historic Armenian schools, the [Melkonian Educational Institute](/wiki/Melkonian_Educational_Institute "Melkonian Educational Institute") established in 1926 which operated until 2005. The Melkonian Institution was created as an orphanage in the aftermath of the [Armenian Genocide](/wiki/Armenian_Genocide "Armenian Genocide") of 1915--1923.  

Economy {#Economy}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Economy")\]

|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg.png) | This section needs to be **updated** . Please help update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information. *(October 2017)* |

[![Photo of Central Bank of Cyprus in Nicosia](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Cyprus_central_bank_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg/220px-Cyprus_central_bank_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg)](/wiki/File:Cyprus_central_bank_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg) [Central Bank of Cyprus](/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Cyprus "Central Bank of Cyprus") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Nicosia_Financial_quarter_just_after_sunset_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg/220px-Nicosia_Financial_quarter_just_after_sunset_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_Financial_quarter_just_after_sunset_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg) View of Nicosia Financial Quarter

Nicosia is the financial and business heart of Cyprus. The city hosts the headquarters of all Cypriot banks, namely the former [Cyprus Popular Bank](/wiki/Cyprus_Popular_Bank "Cyprus Popular Bank") (also known as Laiki Bank), [Bank of Cyprus](/wiki/Bank_of_Cyprus "Bank of Cyprus"), and the [Hellenic Bank](/wiki/Hellenic_Bank "Hellenic Bank"). Further, the [Central Bank of Cyprus](/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Cyprus "Central Bank of Cyprus") is located in the Acropolis area of the Cypriot capital. A number of international businesses base their Cypriot headquarters in Nicosia, such as the big four accounting firms [PWC](/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers "PricewaterhouseCoopers"), [Deloitte](/wiki/Deloitte "Deloitte"), [KPMG](/wiki/KPMG "KPMG") and [Ernst \& Young](/wiki/Ernst_%26_Young "Ernst & Young"). International technology companies such as [NCR](/wiki/NCR_Corporation "NCR Corporation") and [TSYS](/wiki/TSYS "TSYS") have their regional headquarters in Nicosia. The city is also home to local financial newspapers such as the [Financial Mirror](/wiki/Financial_Mirror "Financial Mirror") and Stockwatch. [Cyprus Airways](/wiki/Cyprus_Airways "Cyprus Airways") had its head offices in the entrance of [Makariou Avenue](/wiki/Makariou_Avenue,_Nicosia "Makariou Avenue, Nicosia").^[\[150\]](#cite_note-154)^ The largest mall in Cyprus, [Nicosia Mall](/wiki/Nicosia_Mall "Nicosia Mall"), is located in the city. According to a [UBS](/wiki/UBS "UBS") survey in August 2011, Nicosia is the wealthiest per capita city of the [Eastern Mediterranean](/wiki/Eastern_Mediterranean "Eastern Mediterranean") and the tenth richest city in the world by purchasing power in 2011.^[\[151\]](#cite_note-155)^{#cite_ref-155}  

Transport {#Transport}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Transport")\]  

### Rapid transit {#Rapid_transit}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Rapid transit")\]  

#### Bus transport {#Bus_transport}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Bus transport")\]
[![Photo of buses at Solomou Square in Nicosia](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Solomos_Bus_Station_by_night_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg/220px-Solomos_Bus_Station_by_night_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg)](/wiki/File:Solomos_Bus_Station_by_night_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg) Public buses run by OSEL, in [Solomos Square](/wiki/Solomos_Square "Solomos Square")

Public transport within the district is served by Nicosia Public Transport, a subsidiary of Cyprus Public Transport.^[\[152\]](#cite_note-156)^ Bus service used to be operated by OSEL (Nicosia District Transport Organisation) until 2020, but the company ceased to operate after fraud claims.^[\[153\]](#cite_note-157)^^[\[154\]](#cite_note-158)^{#cite_ref-158}

In the northern part, the company of LETTAŞ provides this service.^[\[155\]](#cite_note-starkblettas-159)^{#cite_ref-starkblettas_159-0}  

#### Train {#Train}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Train")\]

There is no operating train network in Cyprus. Plans for the creation of an intercity railway have been made, but none has materialised. The first railway line on the island was the [Cyprus Government Railway](/wiki/Cyprus_Government_Railway "Cyprus Government Railway") which operated from 1905 to 1951. It was closed down due to financial reasons.^[\[156\]](#cite_note-160)^ It used to stop in the city.{#cite_ref-160}  

### Motorways {#Motorways}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: Motorways")\]

Nicosia is linked with other major cities in Cyprus via a [modern motorway network](/wiki/Roads_and_motorways_in_Cyprus "Roads and motorways in Cyprus"). The [A1 motorway](/wiki/A1_motorway_(Cyprus) "A1 motorway (Cyprus)") to the south, connects Nicosia with [Limassol](/wiki/Limassol "Limassol"), which continues onto the [A6](/wiki/A6_motorway_(Cyprus) "A6 motorway (Cyprus)") going from Limassol to [Paphos](/wiki/Paphos "Paphos"). The [A2](/wiki/A2_motorway_(Cyprus) "A2 motorway (Cyprus)") to the southeast, links Nicosia with [Larnaca](/wiki/Larnaca "Larnaca"), continuing onto the [A3](/wiki/A3_motorway_(Cyprus) "A3 motorway (Cyprus)") going from Larnaca to [Ayia Napa](/wiki/Ayia_Napa "Ayia Napa"). The [A9](/wiki/A9_motorway_(Cyprus) "A9 motorway (Cyprus)") to the west, connects Nicosia to the western Nicosia district villages and the [Troodos mountains](/wiki/Troodos_Mountains "Troodos Mountains"). The [A22 Ring Road](/wiki/A22_motorway_(Cyprus) "A22 motorway (Cyprus)") is currently under construction, which is planned to [bypass](/wiki/Ring_road "Ring road") the city.  

### Airports {#Airports}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=38 "Edit section: Airports")\]

The capital is linked, via road, to the 2 international airports under the Republic's administration, [Larnaca International Airport](/wiki/Larnaca_International_Airport "Larnaca International Airport") (located
approx. 50 km (31 mi) south-east from the city) and [Paphos International Airport](/wiki/Paphos_International_Airport "Paphos International Airport") (
approx. 100 km (62 mi) south-west).
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Nicosia_airport_insite_3.JPG/220px-Nicosia_airport_insite_3.JPG)](/wiki/File:Nicosia_airport_insite_3.JPG) [Nicosia International Airport](/wiki/Nicosia_International_Airport "Nicosia International Airport") interior, 2010

The island's largest airport in the past, [Nicosia International Airport](/wiki/Nicosia_International_Airport "Nicosia International Airport"), ceased commercial operations in 1974, after the [Turkish invasion](/wiki/Turkish_invasion_of_Cyprus "Turkish invasion of Cyprus"). It is located within the Green Line buffer zone, and is used as the headquarters of the [United Nations Peacekeeping Force in Cyprus](/wiki/United_Nations_Peacekeeping_Force_in_Cyprus "United Nations Peacekeeping Force in Cyprus") (UNFICYP).

[Ercan International Airport](/wiki/Ercan_International_Airport "Ercan International Airport") is 13 km (8.1 mi) away from Nicosia. Flights to the airport are banned internationally due to the ongoing [Cyprus dispute](/wiki/Cyprus_problem "Cyprus problem"). Non-stop flights only take place from Turkey, and all planes that fly to Northern Cyprus from other countries have to stop over in Turkey.^[\[157\]](#cite_note-auto1-161)^ The Government of the Republic of Cyprus considers the use of Ercan Airport to enter or exit the island illegal,^[\[158\]](#cite_note-162)^ and could result in facing criminal charges when entering (or exiting) the Republic.{#cite_ref-162}  

### Taxis and trams {#Taxis_and_trams}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: Taxis and trams")\]

In 2010, as part of the Nicosia Integrated Mobility Plan, a pre-feasibility study for a proposed tram network has taken place and sponsored by the Ministry of Communications and Works. The study compared two scenarios, with and without the operation of a tramway in terms of emitted polluting loads.^[\[159\]](#cite_note-163)^{#cite_ref-163}

Many taxi companies operate in Nicosia. Fares are regulated by law and taxi drivers are obliged to use a [taximeter](/wiki/Taximeter "Taximeter").  

### Cycling {#Cycling}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=40 "Edit section: Cycling")\]

In 2011, the Nicosia Municipality introduced the Bike in Action scheme, a [bicycle sharing system](/wiki/Bicycle_sharing_system "Bicycle sharing system") which covers the Greater Nicosia area. The scheme is run by the Inter-Municipal Bicycle Company of Nicosia (DEPL).^[\[160\]](#cite_note-164)^{#cite_ref-164}  

Sports {#Sports}
----------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Sports")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/QNM_2010_-_Start_of_Marathon.jpg/170px-QNM_2010_-_Start_of_Marathon.jpg)](/wiki/File:QNM_2010_-_Start_of_Marathon.jpg) Start of [Quantum Nicosia Marathon](/wiki/Quantum_Nicosia_Marathon "Quantum Nicosia Marathon") 2010 at the [Famagusta Gate](/wiki/Famagusta_Gate "Famagusta Gate") [![Photo of field club tennis court in Nicosia](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Field_club_tennis_courts_in_central_old_part_of_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg/220px-Field_club_tennis_courts_in_central_old_part_of_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg)](/wiki/File:Field_club_tennis_courts_in_central_old_part_of_Nicosia_Republic_of_Cyprus.jpg) Field club tennis courts

[Football](/wiki/Football_(soccer) "Football (soccer)") is the most popular sport in Cyprus, and Nicosia is home of three major teams of the island; [APOEL](/wiki/APOEL_F.C. "APOEL F.C."), [Omonia](/wiki/AC_Omonia "AC Omonia") and [Olympiakos](/wiki/Olympiakos_Nicosia "Olympiakos Nicosia"). APOEL and Omonia are dominant in [Cypriot football](/wiki/Football_in_Cyprus "Football in Cyprus"). There are also many other football clubs in Nicosia and the suburbs. The city also hosts [Çetinkaya](/wiki/%C3%87etinkaya_T%C3%BCrk_S.K. "Çetinkaya Türk S.K."), [Yenicami](/wiki/Yenicami_A%C4%9Fdelen_S.K. "Yenicami Ağdelen S.K."), [Küçük Kaymaklı](/wiki/K%C3%BC%C3%A7%C3%BCk_Kaymakl%C4%B1_T%C3%BCrk_S.K. "Küçük Kaymaklı Türk S.K.") and [Gönyeli](/wiki/G%C3%B6nyeli_S.K. "Gönyeli S.K."), four of the major Turkish Cypriot clubs. Nicosia is also home to [AGBU Ararat Nicosia FC](/wiki/AGBU_Ararat_Nicosia_FC "AGBU Ararat Nicosia FC"), the island's only Armenian FC.

Nicosia is also the home for many clubs for [basketball](/wiki/Basketball "Basketball"), [handball](/wiki/Team_handball "Team handball") and other sports. APOEL and Omonia have basketball and [volleyball](/wiki/Volleyball "Volleyball") sections and [Keravnos](/wiki/Keravnos_B.C. "Keravnos B.C.") is one of the major basketball teams on the island. The Gymnastic Club Pancypria (GSP), the owner of the [Neo GSP Stadium](/wiki/Neo_GSP_Stadium "Neo GSP Stadium"), is one of the major athletics clubs on the island. Also, all teams in the [Futsal](/wiki/Futsal "Futsal") First Division are from Nicosia. In addition, two handball teams, European University and SPE Strovolou, are located in Nicosia.

Nicosia has some of the biggest venues on the island; the [Neo GSP Stadium](/wiki/Neo_GSP_Stadium "Neo GSP Stadium"), with a capacity of 23,400, is the home for the [national team](/wiki/Cyprus_national_football_team "Cyprus national football team"), [APOEL](/wiki/APOEL_F.C. "APOEL F.C."), [Olympiakos](/wiki/Olympiakos_Nicosia "Olympiakos Nicosia") and [Omonia](/wiki/AC_Omonia "AC Omonia"). [Makario Stadium](/wiki/Makario_Stadium "Makario Stadium") has a capacity of 16,000. In the north, the [Nicosia Atatürk Stadium](/wiki/Nicosia_Atat%C3%BCrk_Stadium "Nicosia Atatürk Stadium") has a capacity of 28,000.^[\[161\]](#cite_note-165)^ The [Eleftheria Indoor Hall](/wiki/Eleftheria_Indoor_Hall "Eleftheria Indoor Hall") is the biggest basketball stadium in Cyprus, with a capacity of 6,500 seats, and is the home for the [national team](/wiki/Cyprus_national_basketball_team "Cyprus national basketball team"), [APOEL](/wiki/APOEL_B.C. "APOEL B.C.") and [Omonia](/wiki/AC_Omonia "AC Omonia"). The [Lefkotheo indoor arena](/wiki/Lefkotheo "Lefkotheo") is the volleyball stadium for APOEL and Omonia.{#cite_ref-165}

The [Nicosia Marathon](/wiki/Nicosia_Marathon "Nicosia Marathon") took place in 2010 and 2012, organized by [Athanasios Ktorides Foundation](/wiki/Athanasios_Ktorides_Foundation "Athanasios Ktorides Foundation"), and attracted more than 7,000 participants.^[\[162\]](#cite_note-NM-166)^^[\[163\]](#cite_note-FM-167)^{#cite_ref-FM_167-0}

Nicosia hosted the [2000 ISSF World Cup Final](/wiki/2000_ISSF_World_Cup_Final "2000 ISSF World Cup Final") shotgun shooting events. Also, the city hosted two basketball events; the European Saporta Cup in 1997 and the 2005 [FIBA](/wiki/FIBA "FIBA") Europe [All-Star Game](/wiki/All-Star_Game "All-Star Game") in the [Eleftheria Indoor Hall](/wiki/Eleftheria_Indoor_Hall "Eleftheria Indoor Hall"). Another event that was hosted in Nicosia was the [Games of the Small States of Europe](/wiki/Games_of_the_Small_States_of_Europe "Games of the Small States of Europe") in 1989 and 2009.  

Notable people {#Notable_people}
--------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=42 "Edit section: Notable people")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Christopher_Pissarides.jpg/200px-Christopher_Pissarides.jpg)](/wiki/File:Christopher_Pissarides.jpg) [Christopher A. Pissarides](/wiki/Christopher_A._Pissarides "Christopher A. Pissarides"), Nobel Prize winner in Economics

* [Peter I of Cyprus](/wiki/Peter_I_of_Cyprus "Peter I of Cyprus") (1328--1369), King of Cyprus
* [Kıbrıslı Mehmed Kamil Pasha](/wiki/K%C4%B1br%C4%B1sl%C4%B1_Mehmed_Kamil_Pasha "Kıbrıslı Mehmed Kamil Pasha") (1833--1913), Grand Vizier of the Ottoman Empire
* [Fazıl Küçük](/wiki/Faz%C4%B1l_K%C3%BC%C3%A7%C3%BCk "Fazıl Küçük") (1906--1984), former Vice President of the Republic of Cyprus (1960--1963)
* [Glafkos Klerides](/wiki/Glafkos_Klerides "Glafkos Klerides") (1919--2013), former President of the Republic of Cyprus (1993--2003)
* [Tassos Papadopoulos](/wiki/Tassos_Papadopoulos "Tassos Papadopoulos") (1934--2008), former President of the Republic of Cyprus (2003--2008)
* [Marios Garoyian](/wiki/Marios_Garoyian "Marios Garoyian"), former President of the [House of Representatives of Cyprus](/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_Cyprus "House of Representatives of Cyprus") (2008--2011)
* [Benon Sevan](/wiki/Benon_Sevan "Benon Sevan"), Assistant Secretary-General of the United Nations (1992--2005) and the Head of the [Oil for Food program](/wiki/Oil_for_Food_program "Oil for Food program") (1996--2005)
* [Nicos Tornaritis](/wiki/Nicos_Tornaritis "Nicos Tornaritis"), politician and jurist, member of the House of Representatives and Consultant of the Republic of Cyprus
* [Neoklis Kyriazis](/wiki/Neoklis_Kyriazis "Neoklis Kyriazis") (1877--1956), historian and member of the National Council of Cyprus
* [Alparslan Türkeş](/wiki/Alparslan_T%C3%BCrke%C5%9F "Alparslan Türkeş") (1917--1997), [Turkish nationalist](/wiki/Turkish_nationalism "Turkish nationalism") politician, founder of the [Nationalist Movement Party](/wiki/Nationalist_Movement_Party "Nationalist Movement Party") in Turkey
* [Kutlu Adalı](/wiki/Kutlu_Adal%C4%B1 "Kutlu Adalı") (1935--1996), journalist, poet and socio-political researcher and peace advocate
* [Christopher A. Pissarides](/wiki/Christopher_A._Pissarides "Christopher A. Pissarides"), Nobel Prize winner in Economics
* [Mustafa Djamgoz](/wiki/Mustafa_Djamgoz "Mustafa Djamgoz"), professor of cancer biology at [Imperial College London](/wiki/Imperial_College_London "Imperial College London")
* [Manoug Parikian](/wiki/Manoug_Parikian "Manoug Parikian") (1920--1987), violinist and violin professor in the UK
* [Suat Günsel](/wiki/Suat_G%C3%BCnsel "Suat Günsel") (born 1952), businessman and founder of the [Near East University](/wiki/Near_East_University "Near East University")
* [Nicolas Economou](/wiki/Nicolas_Economou "Nicolas Economou") (1953--1993), concert pianist, composer, arranger, conductor and organizer of music festivals
* [Mick Karn](/wiki/Mick_Karn "Mick Karn") (1958--2011), musician
* [Sevgül Uludağ](/wiki/Sevg%C3%BCl_Uluda%C4%9F "Sevgül Uludağ") (born 1958), journalist, activist
* [Alkinoos Ioannidis](/wiki/Alkinoos_Ioannidis "Alkinoos Ioannidis") (born 1969), singer
* [Michalis Hatzigiannis](/wiki/Michalis_Hatzigiannis "Michalis Hatzigiannis") (born 1978), singer
* [Michael Bisping](/wiki/Michael_Bisping "Michael Bisping") (born 1979), mixed martial artist
* [Diam's](/wiki/Diam%27s "Diam's") (born 1980), French rap singer
* [Stephanie Solomonides](/wiki/Stephanie_Solomonides "Stephanie Solomonides") (born 1982), first Cypriot to reach North and South Poles
* [Giorgos Papadopoulos](/wiki/Giorgos_Papadopoulos_(singer) "Giorgos Papadopoulos (singer)") (born 1985), composer, singer
* [Hovig](/wiki/Hovig_Demirjian "Hovig Demirjian") (born 1989), singer, represented Cyprus at the [Eurovision Song Contest 2017](/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2017 "Eurovision Song Contest 2017")
* [Hazar Ergüçlü](/wiki/Hazar_Erg%C3%BC%C3%A7l%C3%BC "Hazar Ergüçlü") (born 1992), actress on the Turkish drama [Medcezir](/wiki/Medcezir "Medcezir")
* [Aleksandar Vezenkov](/wiki/Aleksandar_Vezenkov "Aleksandar Vezenkov") (born 1995), basketball player
* [Vladimiros Tziortzis](/wiki/Vladimiros_Tziortzis "Vladimiros Tziortzis") (born 1997), racing driver

### Foreign embassies and consulates {#Foreign_embassies_and_consulates}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=51 "Edit section: Foreign embassies and consulates")\]  

#### Nicosia {#Nicosia}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=52 "Edit section: Nicosia")\]  
See also: [List of diplomatic missions in Cyprus](/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_in_Cyprus "List of diplomatic missions in Cyprus")

The Republic of Cyprus hosts an [extensive diplomatic community](/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_in_Cyprus "List of diplomatic missions in Cyprus") in its capital city, Nicosia. At present, Nicosia hosts 42 embassies and 3 high commissions (in **bold** ), 12 consulate generals, 44 consulates and 2 vice consulates (in *italics* ), and 1 representation office.^[\[170\]](#cite_note-174)^^[\[171\]](#cite_note-Cy.MFA-DL24-175)^ Do note that some nations might have multiple diplomatics missions in Nicosia.{#cite_ref-Cy.MFA-DL24_175-0}

#### North Nicosia {#North_Nicosia}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=53 "Edit section: North Nicosia")\]  
See also: [List of diplomatic missions in Northern Cyprus](/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_in_Northern_Cyprus "List of diplomatic missions in Northern Cyprus")

The *[de facto](/wiki/De_facto "De facto")* unrecognised state of [Northern Cyprus](/wiki/Northern_Cyprus "Northern Cyprus") hosts a [limited diplomatic community](/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_in_Cyprus "List of diplomatic missions in Cyprus") in its capital in the *de facto* northern part of Nicosia. Foreign missions located in North Nicosia are:^[\[173\]](#cite_note-178)^{#cite_ref-178}  
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg.png) [Australia](/wiki/Australia "Australia") (High Commission Office)^[\[174\]](#cite_note-179)^{#cite_ref-179}
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/23px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png) [EU](/wiki/European_Union "European Union") ([Programme Support Office](/wiki/European_Union%E2%80%93Northern_Cyprus_relations#Aid_programme "European Union–Northern Cyprus relations"))^[\[175\]](#cite_note-180)^{#cite_ref-180}
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png) [France](/wiki/France "France") (Cultural Office)^[\[176\]](#cite_note-181)^{#cite_ref-181}
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png) [Germany](/wiki/Germany "Germany") (Embassy Office)^[\[177\]](#cite_note-182)^{#cite_ref-182}
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/23px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png) [Italy](/wiki/Italy "Italy") (Embassy Office)
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png) [Russia](/wiki/Russia "Russia") (Embassy Office)
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/23px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png) [Turkey](/wiki/Turkey "Turkey") ([Embassy](/wiki/Embassy_of_Turkey_in_the_Turkish_Republic_of_Northern_Cyprus "Embassy of Turkey in the Turkish Republic of Northern Cyprus"))^[\[178\]](#cite_note-183)^{#cite_ref-183}
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png) [United Kingdom](/wiki/United_Kingdom "United Kingdom") (High Commission Office)^[\[179\]](#cite_note-184)^{#cite_ref-184}
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Flag_of_the_United_States_%2823px%29.png/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States_%2823px%29.png) [United States](/wiki/United_States "United States") (Ambassadorship Office)^[\[180\]](#cite_note-185)^{#cite_ref-185}

Notes {#Notes}
--------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Nicosia&action=edit&section=55 "Edit section: Notes")\]  
1. **[\^](#cite_ref-Population_8-0)** South Nicosia's urban area includes the municipalities of Nicosia (south), [Agios Dometios](/wiki/Agios_Dometios "Agios Dometios"), [Egkomi](/wiki/Egkomi "Egkomi"), [Strovolos](/wiki/Strovolos "Strovolos"), [Aglantzia](/wiki/Aglantzia "Aglantzia"), [Lakatameia](/wiki/Lakatameia "Lakatameia"), [Anthoupolis](/wiki/Anthoupolis "Anthoupolis"), [Latsia](/wiki/Latsia "Latsia") and [Yeri](/wiki/Yeri,_Cyprus "Yeri, Cyprus"). The north's includes [North Nicosia](/wiki/North_Nicosia "North Nicosia"), [Gönyeli](/wiki/G%C3%B6nyeli "Gönyeli"), [Gerolakkos](/wiki/Gerolakkos "Gerolakkos") and [Kanli](/wiki/Kanli "Kanli").{#cite_note-Population-8}
{#cite_note-Population-8}
2. **[\^](#cite_ref-9)** [/ˌnɪkəˈsiːə/](/wiki/Help:IPA/English "Help:IPA/English"){#cite_note-9}
{#cite_note-9}
3. **[\^](#cite_ref-10)** [Greek](/wiki/Greek_language "Greek language"): [Λευκωσία](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CE%9B%CE%B5%CF%85%CE%BA%CF%89%CF%83%CE%AF%CE%B1 "wikt:Λευκωσία"); pronounced [\[lɛfko'siɐ\]](/wiki/Help:IPA/Greek "Help:IPA/Greek"){#cite_note-10}
{#cite_note-10}
4. **[\^](#cite_ref-11)** [Turkish](/wiki/Turkish_language "Turkish language"): pronounced [\[lefkoʃa\]](/wiki/Help:IPA/Turkish "Help:IPA/Turkish"){#cite_note-11}
{#cite_note-11}
5. \^ [^***a***^](#cite_ref-HCIN_176-0) [^***b***^](#cite_ref-HCIN_176-1) [^***c***^](#cite_ref-HCIN_176-2) Member-state of the [Commonwealth of Nations](/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations "Commonwealth of Nations"). As such, their embassies to other [commonwealth](/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations "Commonwealth of Nations") members are formally termed as "high commissions".{#cite_note-HCIN-176}
{#cite_note-HCIN-176}

It is fitting that the youths' movement is on Ledra Street, a bustling thoroughfare where the first seeds of Cyprus's separation were sown in the 1950s.{#cite_note-60}

The EOKA rebelled against the British colonial government on April 1, 1955. EOKA insurgents attacked police stations in Nicosia and Kyrenia on June 19, 1955. One individual was killed and fourteen individuals were injured in an explosion near the Central Police Station in Nicosia on June 21, 1955... Turkish Cypriots demonstrated against the British colonial government in Nicosia on January 27--29, 1958. Seven Turkish Cypriots were killed in clashes with British soldiers in Nicosia on January 27, 1958.{#cite_note-61}
